Spectroscopic measurements are obtained for 26 lensed images, including a distant galaxy at z=5.4. Redshifts have been determined for 5 out of 7 multiple-image systems. Through a careful modeling of the mass distribution in the strongly lensed regime, we derive a mass estimate of 5.3\u00d710<SUP>14</SUP> M<SUB>solar</SUB> within 500 kpc. Our mass model is then used to constrain the redshift distribution of the remaining multiply imaged and singly imaged sources. This enables us to examine the physical properties for a subsample of 7 Ly\u03b1 emitters at 1.7<~z<~5.5, whose unlensed luminosities of ~=10<SUP>41</SUP> ergs s<SUP>-1</SUP> are fainter than similar objects found in blank fields. Of particular interest is an extended Ly\u03b1 emission region surrounding a highly magnified source at z=2.6, detected in VIMOS integral field spectroscopy data. The physical scale of the most distant lensed source at z=5.4 is very small (<300 pc), similar to the lensed z~5.6 emitter reported by Ellis et al. in Abell 2218. New photometric data available for Abell 2218 allow for a direct comparison between these two unique objects. Our survey illustrates the practicality of using lensing clusters to probe the faint end of the z~2-5 Ly\u03b1 luminosity function in a manner that is complementary to blank-field narrowband surveys. <P />Data presented herein were obtained at the W. M. Keck Observatory, which is operated as a scientific partnership among the California Institute of Technology, the University of California and the National Aeronautics and Space Administration. Spectroscopic measurements are obtained for 26 lensed images, including a distant galaxy at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.4</F></FORMULA>-->. Redshifts have been determined for 5 out of 7 multiple&hyphen;image systems. Through a careful modeling of the mass distribution in the strongly lensed regime, we derive a mass estimate of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$5.3\\times 10^{14}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>5.3&amp;times;10<SUP>14</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub> within 500 kpc. Our mass model is then used to constrain the redshift distribution of the remaining multiply imaged and singly imaged sources. This enables us to examine the physical properties for a subsample of 7 Ly&alpha; emitters at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$1.7\\lesssim z\\lesssim 5.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>1.7&amp;lsim;z&amp;lsim;5.5</F></FORMULA>-->, whose unlensed luminosities of &sime;10<sup>41</sup> ergs s<sup>&minus;1</sup> are fainter than similar objects found in blank fields. Of particular interest is an extended Ly&alpha; emission region surrounding a highly magnified source at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=2.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=2.6</F></FORMULA>-->, detected in VIMOS integral field spectroscopy data. The physical scale of the most distant lensed source at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.4</F></FORMULA>--> is very small (&lt;300 pc), similar to the lensed <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.6</F></FORMULA>--> emitter reported by Ellis et al. in Abell 2218. New photometric data available for Abell 2218 allow for a direct comparison between these two unique objects. <email xlink:href=\"mailto:soucail@ast.obs-mip.fr\">soucail@ast.obs&hyphen;mip.fr</email>.</p>\n</fn></fn-group>\n</notes>\n</front>\n<body>\n<sec id=\"sc1\">\n<label>1.<x> </x></label>\n<title>INTRODUCTION</title>\n<p>The central regions of massive galaxy clusters act as powerful gravitational telescopes, magnifying the light from background galaxies via the effect of strong lensing. Such magnifications can attain typical values of 1&ndash;3 mag in concentrated cluster cores, enabling the detection of intrinsically fainter sources than in unlensed field surveys. The detailed study of low&hyphen;luminosity galaxies at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;2</F></FORMULA>-->, where the major fraction of star formation activity is thought to occur, is an interesting, but poorly understood topic. Such galaxies can be found either through their Ly&alpha; emission (e.g., Franx et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf22\">1997</xref>; Santos et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf57\">2004</xref>) or through their ultraviolet continuum fluxes via Lyman break techniques (Kneib et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf37\">2004</xref>; Richard et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf54\">2006</xref>).</p>\n<p>A prerequisite for strong&hyphen;lensing studies of intrinsically faint galaxies at high redshift is an accurate measurement of the projected mass distribution in the lens (Kneib et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf39\">2003</xref>; Gavazzi et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf25\">2003</xref>; Sand et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf56\">2005</xref>). Such mass models are primarily limited by the number of available multiply imaged sources of known redshift. Only a few well&hyphen;studied clusters, such as Abell 1689 (Broadhurst et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf8\">2005</xref>; Halkola et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf27\">2006</xref>; Limousin et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf45\">2007</xref>), with more than 30 multiply imaged systems, or Abell 2218 (Ebbels et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf16\">1996</xref>; Kneib et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf38\">1996</xref>) have sufficient constraints to permit precise modeling of each individual dark matter clump.</p>\n<p>Spectroscopic searches for Ly&alpha; emitters (LAEs) at high redshift usually have a better line flux sensitivity and span a larger redshift range (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\Delta z\\sim 4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;Delta;z&amp;sim;4</F></FORMULA>-->) than those of wide&hyphen;field narrowband surveys. This gain in sensitivity is even larger in strong&hyphen;lensing applications. Lensed spectroscopic surveys may also be sensitive to sources with emission lines with an equivalent width <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$W< 20$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>W&amp;lt;20</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;, smaller than those in narrowband surveys (e.g., Fynbo et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf23\">2003</xref>; Shimasaku et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf60\">2006</xref>). An additional complication in narrowband surveys is how interlopers are treated; confirmatory spectroscopy is usually necessary. By contrast, in lensed surveys, the geometric configuration of multiply imaged systems can reliably distinguish between high&hyphen;redshift objects and low&hyphen;redshift interlopers (see e.g., Ellis et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>).</p>\n<p>As our surveys expand, a variety of types of emission&hyphen;line galaxies are being discovered. Of particular interest are the extended Ly&alpha; emission sources, which have been mainly discovered in regions of significant overdensity through deep narrowband imaging (Steidel et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf67\">2000</xref>; Francis et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf21\">2001</xref>). Matsuda et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf46\">2004</xref>) have identified a large number of such giant Ly&alpha; blobs (with typical sizes &gt;50 kpc) in a <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$34^{\\prime }\\times 27^{\\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>34<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;27<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> field of view, demonstrating the existence of a continuous distribution. The origin of the extended Ly&alpha; emission in such radio&hyphen;quiet sources may be explained by gas inflow during the early stages of galaxy formation: large amounts of hydrogen collapsing into the dark matter potential well will cool through Ly&alpha; radiation. Giant Ly&alpha; blobs may thus be the progenitors of very massive galaxies in the local universe. A key issue is whether the same process is seen to occur in lower mass objects. A route to addressing this question is to examine the nature of smaller extended Ly&alpha; sources, either by long&hyphen;slit or integral field spectroscopy (IFS). This identification is more easily accomplished in strongly lensed sources, where magnification will stretch the observed physical scales.</p>\n<p>The spatial magnification associated with lensing can also be used to yield physical sizes for the most distant sources. Using strong lensing in the cluster Abell 2218, Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>) located a remarkably small source at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.6</F></FORMULA>-->, where the combination of the Ly&alpha; emission&hyphen;line flux density and the weak stellar continuum were used to deduce a young age and modest stellar mass (&sime;10<sup>6</sup>&ndash;10<sup>7</sup> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub>) consistent, perhaps, with a forming globular cluster. Further surveys are required to evaluate whether such systems are common at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\simeq 6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sime;6</F></FORMULA>-->.</p>\n<p>The major drawback arising from the study of lensed sources located through studies of individual clusters is, of course, the significant cosmic variance that is associated with the small volumes being probed. Compared to field surveys, any statistical inferences about the abundances of various classes of populations may be much more uncertain, even granting that fainter sources are probed. To overcome this limitation, an effective survey would have to be conducted through a large sample (&sime;20&ndash;40) of lensing clusters, each with reliable mass models based on the spectroscopic study of many multiply imaged systems (Kneib et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf38\">1996</xref>). Fortunately, the construction of such a sample of well&hyphen;mapped clusters is now a realistic proposition. Several <italic>Hubble Space Telescope</italic> (<italic>HST</italic>) snapshot imaging surveys of X&hyphen;ray&ndash;luminous clusters are now underway with associated ground&hyphen;based spectroscopy, such as the Massive Clusters Survey (MACS; GO 10491, P.I.: H. Ebeling) and the Local Cluster Substructure Survey (LoCuSS; GO 10881, P.I.: G. Smith).</p>\n<p>The purpose of this paper is to illustrate the promise of such surveys by examining spectroscopically the rich population of lensed sources located in the lensing cluster Abell 68 (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\alpha =00^{\\mathrm{h}\\,}37^{\\mathrm{m}\\,}06.81^{\\mathrm{s}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;alpha;=00<SUP><RM>h</RM></SUP>37<SUP><RM>m</RM></SUP>06.81<SUP><RM>s</RM></SUP></F></FORMULA>-->, <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\delta =+09^{\\circ }09^{\\prime }24.0^{\\prime \\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;delta;=+09<SUP>&amp;j0;</SUP>09<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>24.0<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> (J2000.0), <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=0.255$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=0.255</F></FORMULA>-->), one of the most X&hyphen;ray&ndash;luminous clusters (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$L_{\\mathrm{X}\\,}\\sim 8.4\\pm 2.3\\times 10^{44}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>L<INF><RM>X</RM></INF>&amp;sim;8.4&amp;plusmn;2.3&amp;times;10<SUP>44</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> ergs s<sup>&minus;1</sup>, 0.1&ndash;2.4 keV) in the X&hyphen;ray brightest Abell&hyphen;type clusters sample (XBACS; Ebeling et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf17\">1996</xref>). Strong lensing in this cluster has been previously studied by Smith et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">2005</xref>, hereafter <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>), as part of a survey of 10 X&hyphen;ray&ndash;luminous galaxy clusters at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 0.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;0.2</F></FORMULA>-->. Smith et al. identified a list of potential multiple&hyphen;image systems, a few of which were confirmed spectroscopically. Here we significantly extend this work by securing the redshifts of new multiple&hyphen;image systems, many of which are strongly lensed LAEs at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\gtrsim 2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gsim;2</F></FORMULA>-->. The combination of a large magnification factor, high&hyphen;resolution <italic>HST</italic> imaging, and broadband photometry enables us to demonstrate the value of studying the physical properties of these faint emitters, such as their star formation rates, intrinsic scales, and stellar masses. The paper is intended to illustrate the significant promise of continuing such spectroscopic work with the larger samples of clusters now being surveyed with <italic>HST</italic>.</p>\n<p>The paper is organized as follows. In <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc2\">&sect; 2</xref>, we describe the various observations and the reduction of the spectroscopic data. We present in <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3\">&sect; 3</xref> the strong&hyphen;lensing constraints, in the light of the redshifts and identification of new multiply imaged systems. <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc4\">Section 4</xref> presents a mass model of the cluster from which the source magnifications are deduced. The physical properties of the various categories of high&hyphen;redshift LAEs are presented in <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc5\">&sect; 5</xref>, and the implications are discussed in the context of the limitations of blank&hyphen;field surveys in <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc6\">&sect; 6</xref>. We summarize our conclusions in <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc7\">&sect; 7</xref>.</p>\n<p>Throughout this paper, we adopt the following cosmology: a flat &Lambda;&hyphen;dominated universe with the values <inline-formula><tex-math colname=\"7\" colsep=\"0\" rowsep=\"1\" align=\"center\" valign=\"top\">0.48</oasis:entry>\n</oasis:row>\n</oasis:tbody>\n</oasis:tgroup>\n</oasis:table>\n<table-wrap-foot>\n<p>Notes.&mdash;The table presents properties of the photometric data set. Col. (1): Instrument; col. (2): filter; col. (3): total integration time; col. (4): pixel size; col. (5): photometric depth (defined as 4 pixels above 3 &sigma;, where &sigma; stands for the typical local background noise); col. (6): photometric correction <italic>C</italic><sub>AB</sub> between the AB and Vega systems; col. (7): seeing measured on bright unsaturated stars.</p>\n</table-wrap-foot>\n</table-wrap></p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2\">\n<label>2.<x> </x></label>\n<title>OBSERVATIONS AND DATA REDUCTION</title>\n<p>We present in this section the photometric and spectroscopic data sets used to assemble our catalog. High&hyphen;resolution images are crucial for the morphological identification of multiple&hyphen;image systems and the precise astrometric position of the sources studied here, whereas multicolor images are used to estimate their spectral energy distributions (SEDs). Redshift and emission&hyphen;line measurements for individual objects were obtained during subsequent spectroscopic observations. These included multiobject spectroscopy of multiply imaged candidates, as well as systematic long&hyphen;slit searches in the central regions of the cluster. <xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg1\">Figure 1</xref> shows the location of the main spectroscopic settings in the cluster field.<fig-group content-type=\"figgrp\" id=\"fg1\" position=\"float\" seq=\"1\">\n<label>Fig. 1.<x>&mdash;</x></label>\n<caption><p>Composite CFH12k&hyphen;<italic>BRI</italic> color image of the field of view around the center of Abell 68. We overplot the redshift measurements obtained for galaxies located in the background of the cluster (<italic>black</italic> <italic>labels</italic>). Red circles represent cluster members confirmed with spectroscopy. We delineate the imprints of the <italic>HST</italic> WFPC2 (<italic>black</italic> <italic>polygon</italic>) and the VIMOS/IFU (<italic>blue</italic> <italic>square</italic>) fields, as well as the spatial coverage of the different LRIS long&hyphen;slit configurations (<italic>red</italic> <italic>rectangles</italic>).</p>\n</caption>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg1_online.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n</fig-group></p>\n<sec id=\"sc2.1\">\n<label>2.1.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Imaging Data</title>\n<p>A considerable body of multiwavelength data exists in the field around Abell 68, including high&hyphen;resolution <italic>HST</italic> imaging. The main characteristics of the data set used in this study are summarized in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb1\">Table 1</xref>. We obtained <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$3\\times 2.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>3&amp;times;2.5</F></FORMULA>--> ks of integration time with the Wide Field Planetary Camera (WFPC2) during Cycle 8 in the <italic>R</italic> F702W band, as part of <italic>HST</italic> program 8249 (PI: J. P. Kneib). Observations were carried out in low&hyphen;sky mode, and a 1.0<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> dithering pattern was used between each exposure. Details on the reduction of these data are given in <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>.</p>\n<p>Recognition of faint multiply imaged systems in the vicinity of the cluster core is hindered by the dominant stellar halo of the brightest cluster galaxy (BCG). To overcome this, we fitted and subtracted from the <italic>HST</italic> image a model representation of the surface brightness distribution using the IRAF task <monospace>ellipse</monospace>. Both the position angle and ellipticity were allowed to vary as a function of the semimajor axis in the fitted elliptical isophotes, as well as the isophote centroid in the central part. This procedure was found to give satisfactory residuals at the center (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg3\">Fig. 3</xref>).</p>\n<p>Associated optical images in <italic>B</italic>, <italic>R</italic>, and <italic>I</italic> have been obtained on UT 1999 November 19 using the CFH12k camera at CFHT. These sample a field of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$42^{\\prime }\\times 28^{\\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>42<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;28<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> at a 0.205<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> pixel scale. The total exposure times are 8.1, 7.2, and 3.6 ks in the <italic>B</italic>, <italic>R</italic>, and <italic>I</italic> band, respectively. The data were reduced using procedures similar to those described by Czoske (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf15\">2002</xref>) and Bardeau et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf3\">2005</xref>).</p>\n<p>At longer wavelengths, Abell 68 has been observed at the Very Large Telescope (VLT) using the Focal Reducer/low&hyphen;dispersion Spectrograph (FORS2/UT4) in the <italic>z</italic>&hyphen;band on UT 2002 October 6 and the Infrared Spectrometer And Array Camera (ISAAC/UT1) in the <italic>J</italic> and <italic>H</italic> bands on UT 2002 September 29. The field of view of the FORS2 image is <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$7.2^{\\prime }\\times 7.2^{\\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>7.2<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;7.2<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> after dithering, with a pixel size of 0.252<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>, and we used 80 dithered exposures of 120 s. The field of view of the ISAAC images is about <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2.5^{\\prime }\\times 2.5^{\\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2.5<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;2.5<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> after dithering, with a pixel size of 0.148<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>, the subintegration&times;integration times of the dithered exposures were <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$6\\times 35$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>6&amp;times;35</F></FORMULA>--> s and <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$10\\times 12$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>10&amp;times;12</F></FORMULA>--> s in the <italic>J</italic> and <italic>H</italic> bands, respectively. All these data have been reduced using procedures similar to those described by Richard et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf54\">2006</xref>).</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2.2\">\n<label>2.2.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Keck Multiobject Spectroscopy</title>\n<p>The Low Resolution Imaging Spectrograph (LRIS; Oke et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf52\">1995</xref>) on Keck I has been used in multiobject (MOS) mode during two observing runs, in order to target background galaxies and multiply imaged candidates selected on the basis of morphology and colors. On UT 2001 August 4, four exposures of 1.8 ks were acquired with a 31 slit mask, using a 300 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grism blazed at 5000 &Aring; in the single red channel of the camera, which covers the approximate range 5500&ndash;9900 &Aring; at a dispersion of 2.5 &Aring; per pixel. The average seeing was &sim;1.0<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>. The night was photometric, and spectrophotometric standard stars were used for flux calibration.</p>\n<p>On UT 2002 November 30, a 32 slit mask was used during <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$3\\times 2.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>3&amp;times;2.4</F></FORMULA>--> ks of integration time. A 6800 &Aring; dichroic separated the red channel of the instrument, equipped with a 600 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grating blazed at 7500 &Aring;, from the blue channel equipped with a 400 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grism blazed at 3400 &Aring;. The whole setting covers the wavelength range 3500&ndash;9500 &Aring; with dispersions of 1.28 and 1.09 &Aring; per pixel in the red and blue channels, respectively. Despite good seeing conditions (&sim;0.8<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>), the night was not photometric, and no standard stars were observed. These data sets were reduced using standard IRAF procedures for bias removal, flat&hyphen;fielding, wavelength and flux calibration, sky subtraction, and extraction of the one&hyphen;dimensional spectra.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2.3\">\n<label>2.3.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Keck Long&hyphen;Slit Spectroscopy</title>\n<sec id=\"sc2.3.1\">\n<label>2.3.1.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Optical Spectroscopy</title>\n<p>Abell 68 was observed on UT 2002 September 11 with LRIS, in the course of a survey targeting low&hyphen;luminosity Ly&alpha; sources at high redshift (Santos et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf57\">2004</xref>). A 175<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> long and 1<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> wide slit was used to map the high&hyphen;magnification regions of a sample of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 0.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;0.2</F></FORMULA>--> lensing clusters. In the case of Abell 68, six adjacent slit settings scanned the theoretical location of the critical lines at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5</F></FORMULA>-->, with <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2\\times 1000$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2&amp;times;1000</F></FORMULA>--> s of integration time at each position. The reduction of these data is detailed in Santos et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf57\">2004</xref>).</p>\n<p>In addition to the detection of high&hyphen;redshift sources through their Ly&alpha; emission, this blind spectroscopic survey provided secure redshifts for a number of lensed background galaxies serendipitously falling into the long slit. On UT 2003 August 26, a single long&hyphen;slit LRIS position was aligned on two components of a triply imaged system, discovered as <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;dropouts by a <italic>RIz</italic> color&hyphen;color selection technique (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3\">&sect; 3</xref>). A 300 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grism blazed at 5000 &Aring; and a 600 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grating blazed at 1&mu;m were used in the blue and red channels of the instrument, both light paths being separated by a dichroic at 6800 &Aring;. Two exposures of 1.2 ks were acquired at this position, with a 5<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> dithering offset along the slit. Finally, an additional LRIS long&hyphen;slit integration of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$3\\times 1.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>3&amp;times;1.2</F></FORMULA>--> ks was acquired on UT 2005 November 29 with a 600 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grism blazed at 4000 &Aring;, a 400 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grating blazed at 8500 &Aring;, a 5600 &Aring; dichroic, and 5<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> dithering offsets.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2.3.2\">\n<label>2.3.2.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Near&hyphen;Infrared Spectroscopy</title>\n<p>Abell 68 was observed on UT 2005 October 13 using the Near&hyphen;InfraRed SPECtrograph (NIRSPEC; McLean et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf47\">1998</xref>) on Keck II, during a spectroscopic survey of the critical lines of lensing clusters similar to the LRIS survey described before, but at longer wavelengths (Stark &amp; Ellis <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf65\">2006</xref>). A <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$42^{\\prime \\prime }\\times 0.76^{\\prime \\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>42<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;0.76<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> long slit was used at two adjacent slit positions, with <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$9\\times 600$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>9&amp;times;600</F></FORMULA>--> s of integration time on each of them. The spectra were reduced using IDL routines, following optimal spectroscopic reductions techniques presented in Kelson (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf33\">2003</xref>). More details are presented in a forthcoming paper (Stark et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf66\">2007</xref>).</p>\n</sec>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2.4\">\n<label>2.4.<x> </x></label>\n<title>VLT Integral Field Spectroscopy</title>\n<p>Abell 68 was observed on UT 2004 August 12 using the VIsible Multi&hyphen;Object Spectrograph (VIMOS; Le F&egrave;vre et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf43\">2003</xref>) on VLT/UT3 in low&hyphen;resolution (LR&hyphen;blue grism) intregral field spectroscopy (IFS) mode, as part of a survey targeting the central regions of an intermediate&hyphen;redshift galaxy cluster sample (073.A&hyphen;0774; PI: G. Soucail). The <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$54^{\\prime \\prime }\\times 54^{\\prime \\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>54<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;54<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> field of view of the integral field unit (IFU; composed of 6400 fibers, split into four quadrants feeding the four VIMOS CCDs) was centered on the cD galaxy. In the given configuration, the spectral resolution is about 200, and the diameter of the fibers is 0.66<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>, covering the wavelength range 3900&ndash;6800 &Aring; with a dispersion of 5.355 &Aring; per pixel; <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2\\times 2.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2&amp;times;2.4</F></FORMULA>--> ks of integration time were acquired without dithering.</p>\n<p>These three&hyphen;dimensional (3D) spectroscopic data have been reduced using the Vimos Interactive Pipeline Graphical Interface (VIPGI; Scodeggio et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf58\">2005</xref>).<xref ref-type=\"fn\" rid=\"fn11\">11</xref> Before building the data cube for each exposure, every step in the data reduction was performed on a single&hyphen;quadrant basis. After bias subtraction and cosmic&hyphen;ray removal (see Zanichelli et al. [<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf71\">2005</xref>] for a description of the algorithm), the spectra were traced on the CCDs with the help of the high signal&hyphen;to&hyphen;noise ratio (S/N) spectra of a continuum lamp. Following wavelength calibration, inhomogeneities in fiber efficiencies were corrected by measuring the counts in the 5577 &Aring; sky emission line after subtracting the contribution from a galaxy spectrum where fibers cover a galaxy position. The flux calibration is applied by using observations of a standard star in each quadrant. See Covone et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf14\">2006</xref>), who present similar data on Abell 2667, for a detailed description of the procedures.</p>\n<fn-group>\n<fn id=\"fn11\">\n<label>11</label>\n<p>VIPGI has been developed within the VIRMOS Consortium. For more information, see <ext-link ext-link-type=\"uri\" xlink:href=\"http://cosmos.mi.iasf.cnr.it/pandora/vipgi.html\">http://cosmos.mi.iasf.cnr.it/pandora/vipgi.html</ext-link>.</p>\n</fn></fn-group>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2.5\">\n<label>2.5.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Redshift Measurements</title>\n<p>We attempted to measure the redshift of all individual objects falling in the slits that revealed a discernible continuum or possible emission lines. To obtain an accurate redshift measurement for foreground galaxies, cluster members, and other bright objects, we applied the IRAF task <monospace>xcsao</monospace> from the radial velocity package RVSAO (Kurtz et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf41\">1992</xref>) on all extracted spectra. This procedure uses a cross&hyphen;correlation method based on spectral templates (Coleman et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf13\">1980</xref>; Kinney et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf35\">1996</xref>) to estimate the redshift and the corresponding redshift error. For the remaining objects in the spectroscopic catalog, the redshift measurement is based on the wavelength at the peak of the brightest emission line detected. In the latter case, we estimated the redshift error from the spectral dispersion. Additional uncertainties generated by the accuracy of the relative and absolute wavelength calibrations, of about 0.8 and 1.5 &Aring;, respectively, for the LRIS data, were quadratically added to the previous estimates to yield the final redshift errors.</p>\n<p>A confidence class <italic>C</italic>, ranging from 1 to 4, was assigned to each individual redshift measurement according to the prescription of Le F&egrave;vre et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf42\">1995</xref>): this corresponds to a probability level for a correct identification of 50%, 75%, 95%, and 100%, respectively. A specific value of 9 is used when only a single secure spectral feature is seen in emission. The identification of most <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;2</F></FORMULA>--> objects in the catalog is based on only a single emission line interpreted as Ly&alpha; and a confidence class of 9. However, the constraints provided by the lensing configuration in case of multiple images (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3\">&sect; 3</xref>) enable us to strengthen most of these interpretations.</p>\n<p>Multicolor photometry was performed for all sources identified in the WFPC F702W&hyphen;band and CFH12k <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;band images, using the SExtractor software (Bertin &amp; Arnouts <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf4\">1996</xref>). Total magnitudes and errors were measured on the original images without any resampling or convolution. The final spectroscopic catalog of lensed galaxies is presented in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb2\">Table 2</xref>, and individual spectra of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 1$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;1</F></FORMULA>--> sources are shown in <xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg2\">Figure 2</xref>.<table-wrap id=\"tb2\" Long&hyphen;slit and IFU pointings were mainly focused on the central region of the cluster (within &sim;80<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>) in the vicinity of the critical curves, whereas MOS surveys with LRIS probed a wider field of view of &sim;<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$6^{\\prime }\\times 8^{\\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>6<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;8<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>-->.</p>\n<p>The redshift distribution of lensed background galaxies appears to be highly correlated.
