declination are degrees, arcminutes, and arcseconds. In addition to the six secured systems, C10 is included as a potential candidate (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3.1\">&sect; 3.1</xref>). Col. (1): identification; cols. (2)&ndash;(3): astrometric position (J2000.0); cols. (4)&ndash;(6): ellipse shape parameters (<italic>a</italic>, <italic>b</italic>, and \u03b8); col. (7): <italic>R</italic><sub>702W</sub> magnitude; col. (8): measured redshift; col. (9): magnification factor (in magnitudes) derived from the mass model. Bracketed values are also predictions inferred from the mass model.</p>\n<fn id=\"tb3fna\">\n<label>a</label>\n<p>Smith et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf63\">2002a</xref>).</p>\n</fn>\n</table-wrap-foot>\n</table-wrap></p>\n<sec id=\"sc3.1\">\n<label>3.1.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Morphological Identification</title>\n<p>Multiply imaged systems can be identified via a visual inspection of morphologies in the central region of the <italic>HST R</italic><sub>702W</sub> image (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg3\">Fig. 3</xref>), examined in combination with the broadband photometric catalogs. Our starting point is a detailed study of candidates identified to <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu _{702}\\sim 25$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;<INF>702</INF>&amp;sim;25</F></FORMULA>--> mag arcsec<sup>&minus;2</sup> presented by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>. This work revealed three main systems (C0a, b, c; C1a, b, c; and C2a, b), as well as 20 other possible multiply imaged candidates (C3 to C22). We adopt the same nomenclature, extending to include the new systems presented here.</p>\n<p>The three images identified as C15, C16, and C17 have been selected as <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;dropouts on the basis of color&hyphen;color diagrams combining <italic>R</italic>, <italic>I</italic>, and <italic>z</italic>&hyphen;band filters. Indeed, they are very faint in the <italic>HST</italic> image (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$R_{702}\\sim 25.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>R<INF>702</INF>&amp;sim;25.7</F></FORMULA>-->) and undetected at shorter wavelengths in the <italic>B</italic> or <italic>R</italic> band with CFH12k with a combination of red <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$( R-I) _{\\mathrm{AB}\\,}\\sim 1.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;parl0;R-I&amp;parr0;<INF><RM>AB</RM></INF>&amp;sim;1.7</F></FORMULA>--> and blue <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$( I-z) _{\\mathrm{AB}\\,}\\sim -0.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;parl0;I-z&amp;parr0;<INF><RM>AB</RM></INF>&amp;sim;-0.5</F></FORMULA>--> colors, as measured with aperture photometry on the seeing&hyphen;matched images. Such a spectral energy distribution (SED) is characteristic of galaxies in the redshift range <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$5\\lesssim z\\lesssim 6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>5&amp;lsim;z&amp;lsim;6</F></FORMULA>-->, where the Ly&alpha; break in the spectral continuum occurs between the <italic>R</italic> and <italic>I</italic> bands. The preliminary mass model (<xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc4\">&sect; 4</xref>) shows that the location of these three images is compatible with a multiply imaged source, thereby strengthening the high&hyphen;redshift interpretation. We designate this system as C15 (with the three images C15a, b, and c corresponding to C15/16/17) and confirmed that the components C15a and C15b lie at the same redshift using LRIS spectroscopy (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3.2\">&sect; 3.2</xref>).</p>\n<p>The arclet identified as C20 was serendipitously covered during the same LRIS long&hyphen;slit observation. We interpret the extended emission seen in the spectrum (<xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3.2\">&sect; 3.2</xref>) as Ly&alpha; at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=2.689$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=2.689</F></FORMULA>-->. This is also supported by the mass model, which predicts two detected counterimages with similar optical colors. We refer to this system as C20a, b, and c.</p>\n<p>Next to the C20a and C20b images, a fainter extended arc C6 was identified by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref> as a possible multiply imaged system at a similar redshift. This arc can be split into three components, C6a, b, and c.</p>\n<p>Finally, we uncovered a new lensed image, C23a, close to the cluster center during the critical line survey using LRIS (Santos et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf57\">2004</xref>). Its spectrum is consistent with a high&hyphen;redshift source dominated by its Ly&alpha; emission. Again, the cluster mass model predicts the position of a second faint component for this system (C23b), detected on the <italic>HST</italic> image.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc3.2\">\n<label>3.2.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Redshift Constraints</title>\n<p>We now present the new spectroscopic redshifts obtained for six multiply imaged candidates, as well as constraints implied for the remaining multiply imaged systems, C2 and C10, from the updated mass model (<xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc4\">&sect; 4</xref>).<list>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C0 source</italic>.&mdash;This source is a strongly lensed (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu \\sim 3.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;&amp;sim;3.2</F></FORMULA>--> mag) multiply imaged system with three components, discovered during a survey for extremely red objects (EROs) in the fields of 10 massive galaxy cluster lenses at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 0.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;0.2</F></FORMULA>--> (Smith et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf64\">2002b</xref>). A redshift measurement on the brightest image, C0a, was presented in Smith et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf63\">2002a</xref>). Based on the 4000 &Aring; break identification at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\lambda =1.04\\pm 0.01$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;lambda;=1.04&amp;plusmn;0.01</F></FORMULA>--> &mu;m, the redshift is <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=1.60\\pm 0.03$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=1.60&amp;plusmn;0.03</F></FORMULA>-->. This image was also included in two LRIS masks, but we failed to detect strong spectral features in the wavelength range 5500&ndash;9200 &Aring;.</p>\n<p>Because of the clear symmetry of images C0a and C0b with respect to the critical line, it is possible to isolate four bright knots in each of images C0a, C0b, and C0c and use the corresponding 12 images to constrain the mass model. Furthermore, part of the southwest knot of C0a is located within the radial caustic line in the source plane. We are able to detect a very faint radial arc predicted by the mass model (labeled &ldquo;C0&hyphen;radial&rdquo; in <xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg3\">Fig. 3</xref>) after removing the light from the BCG.</p>\n</list-item>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C1 source</italic>.&mdash;The brightest component C1a of this system was observed during our NIRSPEC critical lines survey (see Stark &amp; Ellis <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf65\">2006</xref>; Stark et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf66\">2007</xref>). Three strong emission lines were identified as [O <sc>iii</sc>] &lambda;5007, [O <sc>iii</sc>] &lambda;4959, and H&beta; (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg4\">Fig. 4</xref>, <italic>left</italic>), which unambiguously give the redshift <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=1.583$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=1.583</F></FORMULA>-->. Optical spectroscopy of component C1c, included in one of our LRIS masks, could not identify any strong [O <sc>ii</sc>] emission for this source, with a 3 &sigma; upper limit of 50 &Aring; for the equivalent width in the rest frame.</p>\n</list-item>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C4 source</italic>.&mdash;Although not multiply imaged, this blue arc has very strong Ly&alpha; emission corresponding to <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 2.63$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;2.63</F></FORMULA>-->. An extended Ly&alpha; blob has also been detected in the IFU data (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc5.4\">&sect; 5.4</xref>; <xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg3\">Fig. 3</xref>). The mass model gives a very high magnification factor of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu \\sim 4.0$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;&amp;sim;4.0</F></FORMULA>--> mag, because the source is very close to a cusp.</p>\n</list-item>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C6 and C20 sources</italic>.&mdash;We identify a spatially extended emission line in the LRIS spectrum at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\lambda =4485$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;lambda;=4485</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;, surrounding the C20c image (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg4\">Fig. 4</xref>, <italic>middle</italic>). The lack of other strong emission lines in the optical range and the predicted position for two other components for C20 from the mass model confirms this to be Ly&alpha; at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=2.689$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=2.689</F></FORMULA>-->. In addition, this redshift is close to the Ly&alpha; blob associated with C4, and we identify a similar strong emission line at a similar redshift, <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=2.693$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=2.693</F></FORMULA>-->, for the nearby source C25 (&sim;8<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> away in the source plane).</p>\n<p>The location and color of the lower surface brightness arc, C6, close to images C20a and C20b, is compatible with three merging images forming a single giant arc at a similar redshift (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg4\">Fig. 4</xref>, <italic>middle</italic>). This is further evidence of a possible group of galaxies at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 2.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;2.6</F></FORMULA>--> including sources C6, C20, and C25.</p>\n<p><italic>C15 source</italic>.&mdash;A strong asymmetric emission line is clearly seen on the LRIS spectrum at the position of C15a and C15b (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg4\">Fig. 4</xref>, <italic>top right</italic>), with a central peak at 7808 &Aring;. In both cases, a faint continuum is detected on the red side of the emission line, with a flux &sim;<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$( 4.4\\pm 1.5) \\times 10^{-19}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;parl0;4.4&amp;plusmn;1.5&amp;parr0;&amp;times;10<SUP>-19</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> ergs s<sup>&minus;1</sup> cm<sup>&minus;2</sup> &Aring;<sup>&minus;1</sup>. We interpret the emission line as Ly&alpha; at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.421$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.421</F></FORMULA>-->. This redshift could be slightly overestimated due to an unknown amount of self&hyphen;absorption in the Ly&alpha; emission line and the absence of other spectral features. By averaging the extracted spectra of both images (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg4\">Fig. 4</xref>, <italic>top right</italic>), the integrated flux measured within the emission line, of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$( 9.7\\pm 0.8) \\times 10^{-17}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;parl0;9.7&amp;plusmn;0.8&amp;parr0;&amp;times;10<SUP>-17</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> ergs s<sup>&minus;1</sup> cm<sup>&minus;2</sup>, corresponds to a rest&hyphen;frame equivalent width of &sim;35 &Aring;. We measure a full&hyphen;width half&hyphen;maximum of &sim;7 &Aring; when fitting the average emission line with a Gaussian profile. The strong Ly&alpha; emission line of this source seems to dominate the overall <italic>I</italic>&hyphen;band flux.</p>\n</list-item>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C23 source</italic>.&mdash;The identification of the pair of images C23a and C23b, predicted by the lensing model at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=3.1$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=3.1</F></FORMULA>-->, strengthens the Ly&alpha; interpretation for the single emission line seen in the spectrum of C23a at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\lambda =5028$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;lambda;=5028</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;. A fainter counterimage, C23c, predicted by the mass model, lies beyond the detection limit of the <italic>HST</italic> image.</p>\n</list-item>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C2 source</italic>.&mdash;This system is composed of two bright symmetrical images, identified close to the cluster center. Using the mass model, we predict a redshift of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 1.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;1.4</F></FORMULA>--> for this source, with a magnification factor of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu \\sim 2.9$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;&amp;sim;2.9</F></FORMULA>--> mag for C2a and C2b. A less magnified (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu \\sim 1.8$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;&amp;sim;1.8</F></FORMULA>--> mag) counterimage, C2c, is also predicted by the model, but is not detected in the less sensitive region of the <italic>HST</italic> image, at the junction between two WF chips.</p>\n</list-item>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C10 source</italic>.&mdash;A faint curved arc near a bright cluster member was identified by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref> as a multiply imaged candidate C10. The optical colors of this blue arc are indeed compatible with a source at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z< 2.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;lt;2.5</F></FORMULA>-->. It is probably formed by two images merging on the critical line; its shape is in agreement with predictions from the mass model. However, the low surface brightness of this arc and the lack of spectroscopic information strongly limit this interpretation, making it more uncertain than the systems previously mentioned. Therefore, we only include this source in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb3\">Table 3</xref> as a possible additional multiply imaged system. The mass model predicts a redshift of &sim;1.1, which is in very good agreement with the photometric redshift estimate of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z_{\\mathrm{phot}\\,}=1.15\\pm 0.05$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z<INF><RM>phot</RM></INF>=1.15&amp;plusmn;0.05</F></FORMULA>--> derived from the broadband colors using the Hyperz photometric redshift code (Bolzonella et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf5\">2000</xref>). A fainter counterimage (C10c) is predicted by the mass model, but remains undetected in the <italic>HST</italic> image.</p>\n</list-item>\n</list>\n<fig-group content-type=\"figgrp\" id=\"fg4\" position=\"float\" seq=\"4\">\n<label>Fig. 4.<x>&mdash;</x></label>\n<caption><p><italic>Left</italic>: NIRSPEC bidimensional spectrum of component C1a, showing the detection of three strong features identified as [O <sc>iii</sc>] and H&beta; emission lines at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=1.583$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=1.583</F></FORMULA>-->, both in positive (<italic>black</italic>) or negative (<italic>white</italic>), due to the dithering offsets used. <italic>Middle</italic>: Location of the LRIS slit and extended Ly&alpha; emission identified around image C20c (<italic>thick ellipse</italic>). Two brighter components, C20a and C20b, are predicted by the mass model, in agreement with the location of the critical line at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=2.68$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=2.68</F></FORMULA>--> (<italic>solid curve</italic>). The shape and colors of the adjacent giant arc C6 are compatible with a similar redshift, suggesting a physical connection between these two sources. <italic>Top right</italic>: Close&hyphen;up of the 2D sky&hyphen;subtracted LRIS spectrum, showing both strong emission lines seen at the position of C15a and C15b. <italic>Bottom right</italic>: Average extracted spectrum of C15, with the same wavelength range, revealing the clear asymmetrical shape of the spectral line. The relative sky background level is presented as a dotted curve.</p>\n</caption>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg4a.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg4b_online.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg4c_online.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n</fig-group></p>\n</sec>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc4\">\n<label>4.<x> </x></label>\n<title>MASS MODEL</title>\n<sec id=\"sc4.1\">\n<label>4.1.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Modeling Method</title>\n<p>Using the new redshift measurements and the identification of further multiply imaged systems, we are now in a position to considerably improve the precision of the mass model presented by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>. In doing so, we will maintain the pseudo&hyphen;isothermal elliptical mass distribution model (PIEMD; Kassiola &amp; Kovner <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf32\">1993</xref>) adopted by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref> to infer the dark matter mass distribution. This parametric method has been used for modeling galaxy clusters, as well as individual galaxies (Covone et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf14\">2006</xref>; Natarajan et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf48\">1998</xref>). It assumes each dark matter clump can be parameterized by a central position, ellipticity <italic>a</italic>/<italic>b</italic>, position angle \u03b8, central velocity dispersion &sigma;<sub>0</sub>, and two characteristic radii, <italic>r</italic><sub>core</sub> and <italic>r</italic><sub>cut</sub>. The total mass of this profile is proportional to <italic>r</italic><sub>cut</sub>&sigma;<sup>2</sup><sub>0</sub>. A more detailed discussion of the validity of this approach, in contrast to alternatives, is given by Limousin et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf45\">2007</xref>).</p>\n<p>The cluster galaxy population is incorporated into the lens model as galaxy&hyphen;scale perturbations to the cluster potential, assuming a scaling relation <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$M/ L=\\mathrm{const}\\,$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>M&amp;solm0;L=<RM>const</RM></F></FORMULA>--> (Brainerd et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf6\">1996</xref> <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>) for all <italic>r</italic><sub>core</sub>, <italic>r</italic><sub>cut</sub>, and &sigma;<sub>0</sub>. This is motivated by the similar Faber &amp; Jackson (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf20\">1976</xref>) scaling relation observed in elliptical galaxies. Following the same procedure as Limousin et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf45\">2007</xref>), we keep the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$r^{*}_{\\mathrm{cut}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>r<SUP>*</SUP><INF><RM>cut</RM></INF></F></FORMULA>--> and <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\sigma ^{*}_{0}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;sigma;<SUP>*</SUP><INF>0</INF></F></FORMULA>--> values corresponding to a <italic>L</italic>* elliptical galaxy as free parameters, while keeping <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$r^{*}_{\\mathrm{core}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>r<SUP>*</SUP><INF><RM>core</RM></INF></F></FORMULA>--> at 0.15 kpc. We select cluster galaxies in the field of Abell 68 by plotting the characteristic cluster red sequences <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$B-R_{702}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>B-R<INF>702</INF></F></FORMULA>--> and <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$R_{702}-K$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>R<INF>702</INF>-K</F></FORMULA>--> in two color&hyphen;magnitude diagrams, keeping the objects pertaining to both red sequences. This reduces the photometric catalog used by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>, containing 69 galaxies with <italic>K</italic>&hyphen;band photometry, to 47 cluster members. This method is more efficient than a single red sequence selection, as we did not select any of the spectroscopically confirmed background or foreground galaxies. As described in <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>, the <italic>K</italic>&hyphen;band photometry was obtained by Balogh et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf2\">2002</xref>) using GIM2D (Simard <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf61\">1998</xref>) to fit the surface brightness profiles of the cluster galaxies. This method gives more accurate results than one could obtain with SExtractor, because SExtractor usually overestimates the local background around the brightest and most extended galaxies.</p>\n<p>In a first attempt at modeling the lens, we adopted the parameters given by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>, who included two dark matter halos. We found that any attempt to reconstruct the mass distribution using a single clump was unable to reproduce the multiply imaged systems accurately, confirming the strong bimodality of this cluster. When incorporating our spectroscopically confirmed multiply imaged systems, a reoptimization is necessary. To do this, we use the new Bayesian optimization method provided by the Lenstool software<xref ref-type=\"fn\" rid=\"fn12\">12</xref> (Kneib <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf36\">1993</xref>; Jullo et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf30\">2007</xref>) so that we can derive error estimates for each optimized parameter. The software optimizes the locations of each system in the source plane, based on the following &chi;<sup>2</sup> estimator, which defines the goodness of the fit:\n<disp-formula id=\"df1\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"df1.eps\"></graphic><!--<DFORMULA ID=\"df1\"><FD><FL>&amp;chi;<SUP>2</SUP>=<SUM ALIGN=\"c\"><LL>i</LL></SUM>&amp;chi;<SUP>2</SUP><INF>i</INF>,</FL></FD><NO>(1)</NO></DFORMULA>--></disp-formula>\nwhere <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\chi ^{2}_{i}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;chi;<SUP>2</SUP><INF>i</INF></F></FORMULA>--> is the same estimator for a given multiply imaged system <italic>i</italic>, constructed by comparing the predicted positions of the <italic>N</italic> observed images in the source plane (<italic>x</italic><sub><italic>i,j</italic></sub>, <italic>y</italic><sub><italic>i,j</italic></sub>) to their barycenter (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$x^{B}_{i}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>x<SUP>B</SUP><INF>i</INF></F></FORMULA>-->, <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$y^{B}_{i}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>y<SUP>B</SUP><INF>i</INF></F></FORMULA>-->):\n<disp-formula id=\"df2\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"df2.eps\"></graphic><!--<DFORMULA ID=\"df2\"><FD><FL>&amp;chi;<SUP>2</SUP><INF>i</INF>=<FR SHAPE=\"built\"><NU>1</NU><DE>N</DE></FR><SUM ALIGN=\"c\"><LL>j=1&amp;ldots;N</LL></SUM><FR SHAPE=\"built\"><NU>&amp;parl0;x<INF>i,j</INF>-x<SUP>B</SUP><INF>i</INF>&amp;parr0;<SUP>2</SUP>+&amp;parl0;y<INF>i,j</INF>-y<SUP>B</SUP><INF>i</INF>&amp;parr0;<SUP>2</SUP></NU><DE>&amp;sigma;<SUP>2</SUP><INF><RM>pos</RM></INF></DE></FR>,</FL></FD><NO>(2)</NO></DFORMULA>--></disp-formula>\nwhere &sigma;<sub>pos</sub> is the uncertainty in measuring the position of each image in the source plane. We use a typical value of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\sigma _{I}=0.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;sigma;<INF>I</INF>=0.2</F></FORMULA>--><sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> for the same uncertainty in the image plane and relate it to &sigma;<sub>pos</sub> with the amplification <italic>A</italic>: <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\sigma ^{2}_{I}=A\\sigma ^{2}_{\\mathrm{pos}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;sigma;<SUP>2</SUP><INF>I</INF>=A&amp;sigma;<SUP>2</SUP><INF><RM>pos</RM></INF></F></FORMULA>-->.</p>\n<p>For its important influence on the position of systems C15 and C20, we choose to optimize the velocity dispersion and the cut radius of the third brightest cluster galaxy. We also optimize the same parameters for the BCG and galaxy 106 (adjacent to image C0c) in order to match the location of all images from the C0 system.</p>\n<p>The associated reduced &chi;<sup>2</sup> is &sim;1.7, with 21 degrees of freedom, and the astrometric error on the position of the predicted multiple images is 0.37<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> in the image plane. The new parameters of the mass model are presented in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb4\">Table 4</xref>. The optimized values are slightly higher than the ones we obtain by using only their luminosity as a parameter for the gravitational potential. However, those values are not sufficiently high to propose a third dark matter clump. As additional confirmation for the quality of the mass model, we also checked that all spectroscopically confirmed background sources for which we did not identify multiple&hyphen;image systems were valign=\"top\">&hellip;</oasis:entry>\n<oasis:entry colname=\"4\" colsep=\"0\" rowsep=\"1\" align=\"center\" valign=\"top\">&hellip;</oasis:entry>\n<oasis:entry colname=\"5\" colsep=\"0\" rowsep=\"1\" align=\"center\" valign=\"top\">&hellip;</oasis:entry>\n<oasis:entry colname=\"6\" colsep=\"0\" rowsep=\"1\" align=\"center\" valign=\"top\">0.15</oasis:entry>\n<oasis:entry colname=\"7\" colsep=\"0\" rowsep=\"1\" align=\"center\" valign=\"top\">18 &plusmn; 5</oasis:entry>\n<oasis:entry colname=\"8\" colsep=\"0\" rowsep=\"1\" align=\"center\" valign=\"top\">179 &plusmn; 13</oasis:entry>\n</oasis:row>\n</oasis:tbody>\n</oasis:tgroup>\n</oasis:table>\n<table-wrap-foot>\n<p>Notes.&mdash;Col. (1): Identification; cols. (2)&ndash;(3): astrometric position relative to the brightest cluster galaxy; cols. (4)&ndash;(7): PIEMD parameters; col. (8): \u03b8 orientation, increasing from north through east. Bracketed values are not optimized.</p>\n</table-wrap-foot>\n</table-wrap></p>\n<p>In comparison with the results from <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>, we have refined the mass model by increasing the number of constrained parameters from 11 to 21, while keeping a similar reduced &chi;<sup>2</sup> value. In particular, we optimized the location of the second dark matter clump, where we have the main differences in the confirmed multiply imaged systems, and constrained individual parameters for two particular galaxies, in addition to the BCG.</p>\n<fn-group>\n<fn id=\"fn12\">\n<label>12</label>\n<p>For more information and to download the latest version of the code, see <ext-link ext-link-type=\"uri\" xlink:href=\"http://www.oamp.fr/cosmology/lenstool\">http://www.oamp.fr/cosmology/lenstool</ext-link>.</p>\n</fn></fn-group>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc4.2\">\n<label>4.2.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Results from the Mass Model</title>\n<p>Our improved mass model of Abell 68 enables us to compute a <italic>lensing</italic> mass of the cluster by integrating the derived surface mass density within a given projected distance <italic>R</italic>. Within a physical radius <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$R< 500$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>R&amp;lt;500</F></FORMULA>--> kpc, we obtain a value <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$M_{\\mathrm{lens}\\,}=( 5.31\\pm 0.17) \\times 10^{14}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>M<INF><RM>lens</RM></INF>=&amp;parl0;5.31&amp;plusmn;0.17&amp;parr0;&amp;times;10<SUP>14</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub>. This is somewhat higher than the value <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$( 4.4\\pm 0.1) \\times 10^{14}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;parl0;4.4&amp;plusmn;0.1&amp;parr0;&amp;times;10<SUP>14</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub> derived by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>. By comparing both models using the individual parameters given in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb4\">Table 4</xref>, this difference arises mainly because of the higher mass of the second dark matter clump, for which we derive higher &sigma;<sub>0</sub> and <italic>r</italic><sub>cut</sub> values compared to <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>. The remaining model parameters (the location, ellipticity, and orientation) lie within 3 &sigma;. We argue that the parameters of the secondary clump are better constrained in our model, given the identification of new multiple images to the northwest of the cluster. The difference with <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref> is further revealed by computing the ratio <italic>M</italic><sub>cen</sub>/<italic>M</italic><sub>tot</sub> between the mass of the central component (with sole contributions from the main clump and the BCG) and the total mass within 500 kpc. We find <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$M_{\\mathrm{cen}\\,}/ M_{\\mathrm{tot}\\,}=0.56\\pm 0.05$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>M<INF><RM>cen</RM></INF>&amp;solm0;M<INF><RM>tot</RM></INF>=0.56&amp;plusmn;0.05</F></FORMULA>-->, lower than the value of 0.68 derived by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>. This strengthens the bimodal nature of Abell 68. Our parameters for the individual contributing galaxies are quite similar to <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>, except for the low <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$r^{*}_{\\mathrm{cut}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>r<SUP>*</SUP><INF><RM>cut</RM></INF></F></FORMULA>--> value, indicating that the halos have a smaller spatial extent.</p>\n<p>Within the uncertainties, we are now able to predict the location and expected fluxes of the counterimages for the observed multiple systems C2, C10, and C23. Furthermore, the model gives us an estimate of the redshift for the multiple systems C2 and C10, which do not yet have spectroscopic measurements. These predictions are summarized in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb3\">Table 3</xref> as bracketed values.</p>\n<p>In the process of the Bayesian optimization, the software computes the magnification factors and the related error estimates for each source included in the spectroscopic catalog or the multiple images catalog. These values are reported in Tables <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb2\">2</xref> and <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb3\">3</xref>, respectively.</p>\n<p>Apart from the multiple&hyphen;image systems described before, all other background sources in our spectroscopic catalog (C4, C7, C8, C12, C14, C24, C25, C26, and C27) are predicted to be singly imaged. This is compatible with our morphological data. For other sources that do not show multiple images (C3, C5, C9, C11, C13, and C18), we use the mass model to predict their maximum redshift <italic>z</italic><sub>max</sub>. As the radius of the critical line increases with source redshift <italic>z</italic><sub><italic>s</italic></sub>, a multiple image is expected if <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z_{s}> z_{\\mathrm{max}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z<INF>s</INF>&amp;gt;z<INF><RM>max</RM></INF></F></FORMULA>-->. These <italic>z</italic><sub>max</sub> values are summarized in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb3\">Table 3</xref> and are consistent with the observed optical colors. Image C18 is predicted to be a single image at any redshift.</p>\n</sec>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc5\">\n<label>5.<x> </x></label>\n<title>PHYSICAL PROPERTIES OF FAINT Ly&alpha; EMITTERS</title>\n<p>Via our spectroscopic campaign and improved mass model, we are now in a position to explore the physical properties and luminosity distribution of a large sample of intrinsically faint <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2< z< 6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2&amp;lt;z&amp;lt;6</F></FORMULA>--> sources. We recognize that the volumes sampled may be unrepresentative, but that our survey illustrates, by example, the promise of more extensive surveys that may soon be possible with larger cluster samples.</p>\n<p>First we selected from our spectroscopic catalog a subsample of seven high&hyphen;redshift sources (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 1.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;1.5</F></FORMULA>-->) that all have clearly detected Ly&alpha; emission lines. The measured rest&hyphen;frame equivalent widths <italic>W</italic> exceed 2 &Aring;, and the majority have <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$W\\gtrsim 10$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>W&amp;gsim;10</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;. By contrast, typical LAEs selected within narrowband surveys have <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$W\\gtrsim 30$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>W&amp;gsim;30</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;. The strong magnification thus gives us insight into the physical properties of these faint LAEs, including the star formation rate, the stellar mass, and the physical scale corresponding to the star&hyphen;forming regions. These physical values are derived and summarized in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb5\">Table 5</xref>.<table-wrap id=\"tb5\" position=\"float\" seq=\"5\">\n<label>TABLE <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 1.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;1.5</F></FORMULA>--> in our sample and compared with the mean values of the source at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim
