Black data points correspond to the compilation of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5</F></FORMULA>--> surveys from Santos et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf57\">2004</xref>), and black curves are more recent fits to the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.7</F></FORMULA>--> luminosity function by Shimasaku et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf60\">2006</xref>). We overplot in blue the number density estimates based on the sample of six LAEs at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$1.7< z< 3.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>1.7&amp;lt;z&amp;lt;3.7</F></FORMULA>-->.</p>\n</caption>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg8_online.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n</fig-group></p>\n<p>An interesting question is the likelihood of finding highly magnified sources at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.5</F></FORMULA>--> like C15 and the source reported by Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>): we can estimate this through the space density of <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;dropouts in our magnified field of view. Based on our photometric <italic>RIz</italic> color&hyphen;color selection technique (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3.1\">&sect; 3.1</xref>), we identified one source in the field of view covered by the <italic>HST</italic> image. Since it is detected at &sim;8 &sigma; level in the <italic>I</italic>&hyphen;band filter, where <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;dropouts are brighter, and has a magnification factor of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu \\sim 2.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;&amp;sim;2.5</F></FORMULA>-->, we computed the effective covolume in the source plane having <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu > 0.75$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;&amp;gt;0.75</F></FORMULA>-->, taking into account the reduction of the surface area due to lensing effects. We derive an effective covolume of 420 Mpc<sup>3</sup>, in the redshift range <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$5< z< 6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>5&amp;lt;z&amp;lt;6</F></FORMULA>--> probed by our set of filters. Assuming Poisson noise statistics, we obtain a rough estimate of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2.4^{+5.4}_{-2.0}\\times 10^{-3}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2.4<SUP>+5.4</SUP><INF>-2.0</INF>&amp;times;10<SUP>-3</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> Mpc<sup>&minus;3</sup> for the number counts of <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;dropouts. Although cosmic variance effects can be quite large when probing such a small volume, this result is in good agreement with the space density of low&hyphen;luminosity Ly&alpha; sources at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5</F></FORMULA>--> on the diagram (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg8\">Fig. 8</xref>) mentioned above.</p>\n<p>From these simple calculations, C15 does not seem to be a serendipitous case of a low&hyphen;luminosity <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5</F></FORMULA>--> LAE, since we would expect to find one such source in the magnified region of the cluster. By observing a larger number of lensed fields, such as the new <italic>HST</italic> clusters imaged by ACS, we could build a more significant sample of similar objects and compare their physical properties.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc7\">\n<label>7.<x> </x></label>\n<title>CONCLUSIONS</title>\n<p>We have performed a spectroscopic analysis of background sources in the field of the massive cluster Abell 68 and identified 26 lensed images in the range <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$0.3< z< 5.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>0.3&amp;lt;z&amp;lt;5.5</F></FORMULA>-->, including seven LAEs at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 1.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;1.7</F></FORMULA>-->. Using the new redshift measurements and identification of new multiple&hyphen;image systems, we perform a precise modeling of the cluster mass distribution with five spectroscopic systems and also predict the redshift and counterimages for two remaining systems. This makes Abell 68 one of the best modeled lensing clusters, along with Abell 1689 and Abell 2218, allowing for the precise measurement of its dark matter distribution.</p>\n<p>We derived the star formation rates, stellar masses, and physical scales for our sample of high&hyphen;redshift LAEs. The broadband luminosities of these objects are comparable to the faint LAEs found in deep narrowband searches, but their equivalent widths are much lower, making them 1&ndash;2 mag fainter in Ly&alpha; luminosity. Two of these sources show a more extended Ly&alpha; emission region, when compared to the stellar continuum in the <italic>HST</italic> image. For one of them, we demonstrated how we use IFU data to probe regions with distinct Ly&alpha; equivalent widths. The stretch provided by lensing enables us to characterize small regions of Ly&alpha; emission that would otherwise be beyond the reach of ground&hyphen;based integral field instruments. Although the large equivalent widths are comparable to giant Ly&alpha; blobs observed around massive forming galaxies, we interpret the small physical scales of these lensed emissions as outflows originating from a central starburst.</p>\n<p>The highest redshift (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.4</F></FORMULA>-->) multiple&hyphen;image source of this sample is very similar to the pair of strongly lensed images identified by Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>) in Abell 2218, in terms of magnification and physical size, albeit being intrinsically more massive and more luminous. We therefore expect to detect it in IRAC images of depth similar to the data presented in Egami et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf18\">2005</xref>) in the first two channels of this instrument. Such measurements would tighten the constraints on the stellar mass of this source by reducing the degeneracies in the other model parameters and also provide additional information on its age and star formation history, when combined with the properties of the Ly&alpha; emission.</p>\n<p>Our survey provides the first tentative indications of the density of faint LAEs at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 3$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;3</F></FORMULA>-->, down to unlensed fluxes of &sim;<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2\\times 10^{41}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2&amp;times;10<SUP>41</SUP></F></FORMULA>-->. Although our survey is not flux limited nor complete in any formal sense, the cumulative Ly&alpha; luminosity function we derive promises a dedicated search for lensed Ly&alpha; emitters through larger samples of well&hyphen;mapped clusters now being surveyed with <italic>HST</italic> and the ability of this approach to complement narrowband searches carried out in blank fields.</p>\n</sec>\n</body>\n<back>\n<ack>\n<sec>\n<title></title><p>We thank the anonymous referee for his/her helpful comments, and acknowledge helpful discussions with Johan Fynbo, Kim Nilsson, Fabrice Lamareille, Mark Swinbank, and Tommaso Treu. J. R. is grateful to Caltech for financial support. The Dark Cosmology Centre is funded by the Danish National Research Foundation. The authors recognize and acknowledge the very significant cultural role and reverance that the summit of Mauna Kea has always had within the indigenous Hawaiian community. We are most fortunate to have the opportunity to conduct observations from this mountain.</p>\n</sec>\n</ack>\n<ref-list type=\"unparsed\">\n<title>REFERENCES</title>\n<ref id=\"rf1\">\n<citation>Ajiki, M., et al. 2003, AJ, 126, 2091</citation>\n</ref>\n<ref id=\"rf2\">\n<citation>Balogh, M. Printed in U.S.A.</copyright-statement>\n<copyright-year>2007</copyright-year>\n<copyright-holder>The American Astronomical Society</copyright-holder>\n</permissions>\n<related-article related-article-type=\"pdf\" xlink:href=\"517875.web.pdf\"></related-article>\n<related-article related-article-type=\"pdf\" xlink:href=\"517875.pdf\"></related-article>\n<abstract>\n<label>ABSTRACT</label>\n<p>We have carried out an extensive spectroscopic survey with the Keck and VLT telescopes, targeting lensed galaxies in the background of the massive cluster Abell 68. Spectroscopic measurements are obtained for 26 lensed images, including a distant galaxy at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.4</F></FORMULA>-->. Redshifts have been determined for 5 out of 7 multiple&hyphen;image systems. Through a careful modeling of the mass distribution in the strongly lensed regime, we derive a mass estimate of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$5.3\\times 10^{14}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>5.3&amp;times;10<SUP>14</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub> within 500 kpc. Our mass model is then used to constrain the redshift distribution of the remaining multiply imaged and singly imaged sources. This enables us to examine the physical properties for a subsample of 7 Ly&alpha; emitters at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$1.7\\lesssim z\\lesssim 5.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>1.7&amp;lsim;z&amp;lsim;5.5</F></FORMULA>-->, whose unlensed luminosities of &sime;10<sup>41</sup> ergs s<sup>&minus;1</sup> are fainter than similar objects found in blank fields. Of particular interest is an extended Ly&alpha; emission region surrounding a highly magnified source at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=2.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=2.6</F></FORMULA>-->, detected in VIMOS integral field spectroscopy data. The physical scale of the most distant lensed source at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.4</F></FORMULA>--> is very small (&lt;300 pc), similar to the lensed <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.6</F></FORMULA>--> emitter reported by Ellis et al. in Abell 2218. New photometric data available for Abell 2218 allow for a direct comparison between these two unique objects. Our survey illustrates the practicality of using lensing clusters to probe the faint end of the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;2</F></FORMULA>-->&ndash;5 Ly&alpha; luminosity function in a manner that is complementary to blank&hyphen;field narrowband surveys.</p>\n</abstract>\n<kwd-group>\n<title>Subject headings:<x> </x></title>\n<kwd>cosmology: observations</kwd><x>&mdash;</x><kwd>galaxies: clusters: individual (A68)</kwd><x>&mdash;</x><kwd>galaxies: high&hyphen;redshift</kwd><x>&mdash;</x><kwd>gravitational lensing</kwd></kwd-group>\n</article-meta>\n<notes>\n<p><italic>Online material: </italic>color figures</p>\n</notes>\n<notes notes-type=\"footnote\">\n<fn-group>\n<fn id=\"fn1\">\n<label>1</label>\n<p>Data presented herein were obtained at the W. M. Keck Observatory, which is operated as a scientific partnership among the California Institute of Technology, the University of California and the National Aeronautics and Space Administration. The Observatory was made possible by the generous financial support of the W. M. Keck Foundation.</p>\n</fn>\n<fn id=\"fn2\">\n<label>2</label>\n<p>Also based on observations collected at the Very Large Telescope (Antu/UT1 and Melipal/UT3), European Southern Observatory, Paranal, Chile (ESO programs 070.A&hyphen;0643 and 073.A&hyphen;0774), the NASA/ESA <italic>Hubble Space Telescope</italic> (program 8249) obtained at the Space Telescope Science Institute, which is operated by AURA under NASA contract NAS5&hyphen;26555, and the Canada&hyphen;France&hyphen;Hawaii Telescope (CFHT), which is operated by the National Research Council of Canada, the Institut National des Sciences de l&rsquo;Univers of the Centre National de la Recherche Scientifique of France, and the University of Hawaii.</p>\n</fn>\n<fn id=\"fn3\">\n<label>3</label>\n<p>Department of Astronomy, California Institute of Technology, Pasadena, CA 91125; <email xlink:href=\"mailto:ejullo@eso.org\">ejullo@eso.org</email>.</p>\n</fn>\n<fn id=\"fn6\">\n<label>6</label>\n<p>INAF&hyphen;Osservatorio Astronomico di Capodimonte, 80131 Naples, Italy; <email xlink:href=\"mailto:giovanni.covone@na.astro.it\">giovanni.covone@na.astro.it</email>.</p>\n</fn>\n<fn id=\"fn7\">\n<label>7</label>\n<p>Dark Cosmology Centre, Niels Bohr Institute, University of Copenhagen, DK&hyphen;2100 Copenhagen; <email xlink:href=\"mailto:marceau@dark-cosmology.dk\">marceau@dark&hyphen;cosmology.dk</email>.</p>\n</fn>\n<fn id=\"fn8\">\n<label>8</label>\n<p>Argelander&hyphen;Institut f&uuml;r Astronomie (Founded by merging of the Institut f&uuml;r Astrophysik und Extraterrestrische Forschung, the Sternwarte, and the Radioastronomisches Institut der Universit&auml;t Bonn), Universit&auml;t Bonn, 53121 Bonn, Germany; <email xlink:href=\"mailto:oczoske@astro.uni-bonn.de\">oczoske@astro.uni&hyphen;bonn.de</email>.</p>\n</fn>\n<fn id=\"fn9\">\n<label>9</label>\n<p>Institute of Astronomy, University of Hawaii, Honolulu, HI 96822; <email xlink:href=\"mailto:ebeling@ifa.hawaii.edu\">ebeling@ifa.hawaii.edu</email>.</p>\n</fn>\n<fn id=\"fn10\">\n<label>10</label>\n<p>Observatoire Midi&hyphen;Pyr&eacute;n&eacute;es, 31000 Toulouse, France; <email xlink:href=\"mailto:soucail@ast.obs-mip.fr\">soucail@ast.obs&hyphen;mip.fr</email>.</p>\n</fn></fn-group>\n</notes>\n</front>\n<body>\n<sec id=\"sc1\">\n<label>1.<x> </x></label>\n<title>INTRODUCTION</title>\n<p>The central regions of massive galaxy clusters act as powerful gravitational telescopes, magnifying the light from background galaxies via the effect of strong lensing. Such magnifications can attain typical values of 1&ndash;3 mag in concentrated cluster cores, enabling the detection of intrinsically fainter sources than in unlensed field surveys. The detailed study of low&hyphen;luminosity galaxies at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;2</F></FORMULA>-->, where the major fraction of star formation activity is thought to occur, is an interesting, but poorly understood topic. Such galaxies can be found either through their Ly&alpha; emission (e.g., Franx et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf22\">1997</xref>; Santos et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf57\">2004</xref>) or through their ultraviolet continuum fluxes via Lyman break techniques (Kneib et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf37\">2004</xref>; Richard et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf54\">2006</xref>).</p>\n<p>A prerequisite for strong&hyphen;lensing studies of intrinsically faint galaxies at high redshift is an accurate measurement of the projected mass distribution in the lens (Kneib et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf39\">2003</xref>; Gavazzi et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf25\">2003</xref>; Sand et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf56\">2005</xref>). Such mass models are primarily limited by the number of available multiply imaged sources of known redshift. Only a few well&hyphen;studied clusters, such as Abell 1689 (Broadhurst et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf8\">2005</xref>; Halkola et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf27\">2006</xref>; Limousin et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf45\">2007</xref>), with more than 30 multiply imaged systems, or Abell 2218 (Ebbels et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf16\">1996</xref>; Kneib et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf38\">1996</xref>) have sufficient constraints to permit precise modeling of each individual dark matter clump.</p>\n<p>Spectroscopic searches for Ly&alpha; emitters (LAEs) at high redshift usually have a better line flux sensitivity and span a larger redshift range (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\Delta z\\sim 4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;Delta;z&amp;sim;4</F></FORMULA>-->) than those of wide&hyphen;field narrowband surveys. This gain in sensitivity is even larger in strong&hyphen;lensing applications. Lensed spectroscopic surveys may also be sensitive to sources with emission lines with an equivalent width <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$W< 20$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>W&amp;lt;20</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;, smaller than those in narrowband surveys (e.g., Fynbo et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf23\">2003</xref>; Shimasaku et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf60\">2006</xref>). An additional complication in narrowband surveys is how interlopers are treated; confirmatory spectroscopy is usually necessary. By contrast, in lensed surveys, the geometric configuration of multiply imaged systems can reliably distinguish between high&hyphen;redshift objects and low&hyphen;redshift interlopers (see e.g., Ellis et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>).</p>\n<p>As our surveys expand, a variety of types of emission&hyphen;line galaxies are being discovered. Of particular interest are the extended Ly&alpha; emission sources, which have been mainly discovered in regions of significant overdensity through deep narrowband imaging (Steidel et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf67\">2000</xref>; Francis et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf21\">2001</xref>). Matsuda et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf46\">2004</xref>) have identified a large number of such giant Ly&alpha; blobs (with typical sizes &gt;50 kpc) in a <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$34^{\\prime }\\times 27^{\\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>34<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;27<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> field of view, demonstrating the existence of a continuous distribution. The origin of the extended Ly&alpha; emission in such radio&hyphen;quiet sources may be explained by gas inflow during the early stages of galaxy formation: large amounts of hydrogen collapsing into the dark matter potential well will cool through Ly&alpha; radiation. Giant Ly&alpha; blobs may thus be the progenitors of very massive galaxies in the local universe. A key issue is whether the same process is seen to occur in lower mass objects. A route to addressing this question is to examine the nature of smaller extended Ly&alpha; sources, either by long&hyphen;slit or integral field spectroscopy (IFS). This identification is more easily accomplished in strongly lensed sources, where magnification will stretch the observed physical scales.</p>\n<p>The spatial magnification associated with lensing can also be used to yield physical sizes for the most distant sources. Using strong lensing in the cluster Abell 2218, Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>) located a remarkably small source at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.6</F></FORMULA>-->, where the combination of the Ly&alpha; emission&hyphen;line flux density and the weak stellar continuum were used to deduce a young age and modest stellar mass (&sime;10<sup>6</sup>&ndash;10<sup>7</sup> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub>) consistent, perhaps, with a forming globular cluster. Further surveys are required to evaluate whether such systems are common at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\simeq 6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sime;6</F></FORMULA>-->.</p>\n<p>The major drawback arising from the study of lensed sources located through studies of individual clusters is, of course, the significant cosmic variance that is associated with the small volumes being probed. Compared to field surveys, any statistical inferences about the abundances of various classes of populations may be much more uncertain, even granting that fainter sources are probed. To overcome this limitation, an effective survey would have to be conducted through a large sample (&sime;20&ndash;40) of lensing clusters, each with reliable mass models based on the spectroscopic study of many multiply imaged systems (Kneib et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf38\">1996</xref>). Fortunately, the construction of such a sample of well&hyphen;mapped clusters is now a realistic proposition. Several <italic>Hubble Space Telescope</italic> (<italic>HST</italic>) snapshot imaging surveys of X&hyphen;ray&ndash;luminous clusters are now underway with associated ground&hyphen;based spectroscopy, such as the Massive Clusters Survey (MACS; GO 10491, P.I.: H. Ebeling) and the Local Cluster Substructure Survey (LoCuSS; GO 10881, P.I.: G. Smith).</p>\n<p>The purpose of this paper is to illustrate the promise of such surveys by examining spectroscopically the rich population of lensed sources located in the lensing cluster Abell 68 (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\alpha =00^{\\mathrm{h}\\,}37^{\\mathrm{m}\\,}06.81^{\\mathrm{s}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;alpha;=00<SUP><RM>h</RM></SUP>37<SUP><RM>m</RM></SUP>06.81<SUP><RM>s</RM></SUP></F></FORMULA>-->, <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\delta =+09^{\\circ }09^{\\prime }24.0^{\\prime \\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;delta;=+09<SUP>&amp;j0;</SUP>09<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>24.0<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> (J2000.0), <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=0.255$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=0.255</F></FORMULA>-->), one of the most X&hyphen;ray&ndash;luminous clusters (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$L_{\\mathrm{X}\\,}\\sim 8.4\\pm 2.3\\times 10^{44}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>L<INF><RM>X</RM></INF>&amp;sim;8.4&amp;plusmn;2.3&amp;times;10<SUP>44</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> ergs s<sup>&minus;1</sup>, 0.1&ndash;2.4 keV) in the X&hyphen;ray brightest Abell&hyphen;type clusters sample (XBACS; Ebeling et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf17\">1996</xref>). Strong lensing in this cluster has been previously studied by Smith et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">2005</xref>, hereafter <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>), as part of a survey of 10 X&hyphen;ray&ndash;luminous galaxy clusters at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 0.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;0.2</F></FORMULA>-->. Smith et al. identified a list of potential multiple&hyphen;image systems, a few of which were confirmed spectroscopically. Here we significantly extend this work by securing the redshifts of new multiple&hyphen;image systems, many of which are strongly lensed LAEs at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\gtrsim 2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gsim;2</F></FORMULA>-->. The combination of a large magnification factor, high&hyphen;resolution <italic>HST</italic> imaging, and broadband photometry enables us to demonstrate the value of studying the physical properties of these faint emitters, such as their star formation rates, intrinsic scales, and stellar masses. The paper is intended to illustrate the significant promise of continuing such spectroscopic work with the larger samples of clusters now being surveyed with <italic>HST</italic>.</p>\n<p>The paper is organized as follows. In <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc2\">&sect; 2</xref>, we describe the various observations and the reduction of the spectroscopic data. We present in <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3\">&sect; 3</xref> the strong&hyphen;lensing constraints, in the light of the redshifts and identification of new multiply imaged systems. <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc4\">Section 4</xref> presents a mass model of the cluster from which the source magnifications are deduced. The physical properties of the various categories of high&hyphen;redshift LAEs are presented in <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc5\">&sect; 5</xref>, and the implications are discussed in the context of the limitations of blank&hyphen;field surveys in <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc6\">&sect; 6</xref>. We summarize our conclusions in <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc7\">&sect; 7</xref>.</p>\n<p>Throughout this paper, we adopt the following cosmology: a flat &Lambda;&hyphen;dominated universe with the values <inline-formula><tex-math The correction values <italic>C</italic><sub>AB</sub> between AB and Vega photometric systems, defined as <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$m_{\\mathrm{AB}\\,}=m_{\\mathrm{Vega}\\,}+C_{\\mathrm{AB}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>m<INF><RM>AB</RM></INF>=m<INF><RM>Vega</RM></INF>+C<INF><RM>AB</RM></INF></F></FORMULA>-->, are reported in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb1\">Table 1</xref> for each filter.
