presents properties of the photometric data set. Col. (1): Instrument; col. (2): filter; col. (3): total integration time; col. (4): pixel size; col. (5): photometric depth (defined as 4 pixels above 3 &sigma;, where &sigma; stands for the typical local background noise); col. (6): photometric correction <italic>C</italic><sub>AB</sub> between the AB and Vega systems; col. (7): seeing measured on bright unsaturated stars.</p>\n</table-wrap-foot>\n</table-wrap></p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2\">\n<label>2.<x> </x></label>\n<title>OBSERVATIONS AND DATA REDUCTION</title>\n<p>We present in this section the photometric and spectroscopic data sets used to assemble our catalog. High&hyphen;resolution images are crucial for the morphological identification of multiple&hyphen;image systems and the precise astrometric position of the sources studied here, whereas multicolor images are used to estimate their spectral energy distributions (SEDs). Redshift and emission&hyphen;line measurements for individual objects were obtained during subsequent spectroscopic observations. These included multiobject spectroscopy of multiply imaged candidates, as well as systematic long&hyphen;slit searches in the central regions of the cluster. <xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg1\">Figure 1</xref> shows the location of the main spectroscopic settings in the cluster field.<fig-group content-type=\"figgrp\" id=\"fg1\" position=\"float\" seq=\"1\">\n<label>Fig. 1.<x>&mdash;</x></label>\n<caption><p>Composite CFH12k&hyphen;<italic>BRI</italic> color image of the field of view around the center of Abell 68. We overplot the redshift measurements obtained for galaxies located in the background of the cluster (<italic>black</italic> <italic>labels</italic>). Red circles represent cluster members confirmed with spectroscopy. We delineate the imprints of the <italic>HST</italic> WFPC2 (<italic>black</italic> <italic>polygon</italic>) and the VIMOS/IFU (<italic>blue</italic> <italic>square</italic>) fields, as well as the spatial coverage of the different LRIS long&hyphen;slit configurations (<italic>red</italic> <italic>rectangles</italic>).</p>\n</caption>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg1_online.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n</fig-group></p>\n<sec id=\"sc2.1\">\n<label>2.1.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Imaging Data</title>\n<p>A considerable body of multiwavelength data exists in the field around Abell 68, including high&hyphen;resolution <italic>HST</italic> imaging. The main characteristics of the data set used in this study are summarized in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb1\">Table 1</xref>. We obtained <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$3\\times 2.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>3&amp;times;2.5</F></FORMULA>--> ks of integration time with the Wide Field Planetary Camera (WFPC2) during Cycle 8 in the <italic>R</italic> F702W band, as part of <italic>HST</italic> program 8249 (PI: J. P. Kneib). Observations were carried out in low&hyphen;sky mode, and a 1.0<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> dithering pattern was used between each exposure. Details on the reduction of these data are given in <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>.</p>\n<p>Recognition of faint multiply imaged systems in the vicinity of the cluster core is hindered by the dominant stellar halo of the brightest cluster galaxy (BCG). To overcome this, we fitted and subtracted from the <italic>HST</italic> image a model representation of the surface brightness distribution using the IRAF task <monospace>ellipse</monospace>. Both the position angle and ellipticity were allowed to vary as a function of the semimajor axis in the fitted elliptical isophotes, as well as the isophote centroid in the central part. This procedure was found to give satisfactory residuals at the center (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg3\">Fig. 3</xref>).</p>\n<p>Associated optical images in <italic>B</italic>, <italic>R</italic>, and <italic>I</italic> have been obtained on UT 1999 November 19 using the CFH12k camera at CFHT. These sample a field of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$42^{\\prime }\\times 28^{\\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>42<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;28<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> at a 0.205<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> pixel scale. The total exposure times are 8.1, 7.2, and 3.6 ks in the <italic>B</italic>, <italic>R</italic>, and <italic>I</italic> band, respectively. The data were reduced using procedures similar to those described by Czoske (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf15\">2002</xref>) and Bardeau et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf3\">2005</xref>).</p>\n<p>At longer wavelengths, Abell 68 has been observed at the Very Large Telescope (VLT) using the Focal Reducer/low&hyphen;dispersion Spectrograph (FORS2/UT4) in the <italic>z</italic>&hyphen;band on UT 2002 October 6 and the Infrared Spectrometer And Array Camera (ISAAC/UT1) in the <italic>J</italic> and <italic>H</italic> bands on UT 2002 September 29. The field of view of the FORS2 image is <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$7.2^{\\prime }\\times 7.2^{\\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>7.2<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;7.2<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> after dithering, with a pixel size of 0.252<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>, and we used 80 dithered exposures of 120 s. The field of view of the ISAAC images is about <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2.5^{\\prime }\\times 2.5^{\\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2.5<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;2.5<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> after dithering, with a pixel size of 0.148<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>, the subintegration&times;integration times of the dithered exposures were <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$6\\times 35$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>6&amp;times;35</F></FORMULA>--> s and <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$10\\times 12$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>10&amp;times;12</F></FORMULA>--> s in the <italic>J</italic> and <italic>H</italic> bands, respectively. All these data have been reduced using procedures similar to those described by Richard et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf54\">2006</xref>).</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2.2\">\n<label>2.2.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Keck Multiobject Spectroscopy</title>\n<p>The Low Resolution Imaging Spectrograph (LRIS; Oke et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf52\">1995</xref>) on Keck I has been used in multiobject (MOS) mode during two observing runs, in order to target background galaxies and multiply imaged candidates selected on the basis of morphology and colors. On UT 2001 August 4, four exposures of 1.8 ks were acquired with a 31 slit mask, using a 300 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grism blazed at 5000 &Aring; in the single red channel of the camera, which covers the approximate range 5500&ndash;9900 &Aring; at a dispersion of 2.5 &Aring; per pixel. The average seeing was &sim;1.0<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>. The night was photometric, and spectrophotometric standard stars were used for flux calibration.</p>\n<p>On UT 2002 November 30, a 32 slit mask was used during <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$3\\times 2.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>3&amp;times;2.4</F></FORMULA>--> ks of integration time. A 6800 &Aring; dichroic separated the red channel of the instrument, equipped with a 600 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grating blazed at 7500 &Aring;, from the blue channel equipped with a 400 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grism blazed at 3400 &Aring;. The whole setting covers the wavelength range 3500&ndash;9500 &Aring; with dispersions of 1.28 and 1.09 &Aring; per pixel in the red and blue channels, respectively. Despite good seeing conditions (&sim;0.8<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>), the night was not photometric, and no standard stars were observed. These data sets were reduced using standard IRAF procedures for bias removal, flat&hyphen;fielding, wavelength and flux calibration, sky subtraction, and extraction of the one&hyphen;dimensional spectra.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2.3\">\n<label>2.3.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Keck Long&hyphen;Slit Spectroscopy</title>\n<sec id=\"sc2.3.1\">\n<label>2.3.1.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Optical Spectroscopy</title>\n<p>Abell 68 was observed on UT 2002 September 11 with LRIS, in the course of a survey targeting low&hyphen;luminosity Ly&alpha; sources at high redshift (Santos et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf57\">2004</xref>). A 175<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> long and 1<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> wide slit was used to map the high&hyphen;magnification regions of a sample of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 0.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;0.2</F></FORMULA>--> lensing clusters. In the case of Abell 68, six adjacent slit settings scanned the theoretical location of the critical lines at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5</F></FORMULA>-->, with <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2\\times 1000$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2&amp;times;1000</F></FORMULA>--> s of integration time at each position. The reduction of these data is detailed in Santos et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf57\">2004</xref>).</p>\n<p>In addition to the detection of high&hyphen;redshift sources through their Ly&alpha; emission, this blind spectroscopic survey provided secure redshifts for a number of lensed background galaxies serendipitously falling into the long slit. On UT 2003 August 26, a single long&hyphen;slit LRIS position was aligned on two components of a triply imaged system, discovered as <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;dropouts by a <italic>RIz</italic> color&hyphen;color selection technique (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3\">&sect; 3</xref>). A 300 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grism blazed at 5000 &Aring; and a 600 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grating blazed at 1&mu;m were used in the blue and red channels of the instrument, both light paths being separated by a dichroic at 6800 &Aring;. Two exposures of 1.2 ks were acquired at this position, with a 5<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> dithering offset along the slit. Finally, an additional LRIS long&hyphen;slit integration of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$3\\times 1.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>3&amp;times;1.2</F></FORMULA>--> ks was acquired on UT 2005 November 29 with a 600 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grism blazed at 4000 &Aring;, a 400 line mm<sup>&minus;1</sup> grating blazed at 8500 &Aring;, a 5600 &Aring; dichroic, and 5<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> dithering offsets.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2.3.2\">\n<label>2.3.2.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Near&hyphen;Infrared Spectroscopy</title>\n<p>Abell 68 was observed on UT 2005 October 13 using the Near&hyphen;InfraRed SPECtrograph (NIRSPEC; McLean et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf47\">1998</xref>) on Keck II, during a spectroscopic survey of the critical lines of lensing clusters similar to the LRIS survey described before, but at longer wavelengths (Stark &amp; Ellis <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf65\">2006</xref>). A <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$42^{\\prime \\prime }\\times 0.76^{\\prime \\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>42<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;0.76<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> long slit was used at two adjacent slit positions, with <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$9\\times 600$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>9&amp;times;600</F></FORMULA>--> s of integration time on each of them. The spectra were reduced using IDL routines, following optimal spectroscopic reductions techniques presented in Kelson (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf33\">2003</xref>). More details are presented in a forthcoming paper (Stark et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf66\">2007</xref>).</p>\n</sec>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2.4\">\n<label>2.4.<x> </x></label>\n<title>VLT Integral Field Spectroscopy</title>\n<p>Abell 68 was observed on UT 2004 August 12 using the VIsible Multi&hyphen;Object Spectrograph (VIMOS; Le F&egrave;vre et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf43\">2003</xref>) on VLT/UT3 in low&hyphen;resolution (LR&hyphen;blue grism) intregral field spectroscopy (IFS) mode, as part of a survey targeting the central regions of an intermediate&hyphen;redshift galaxy cluster sample (073.A&hyphen;0774; PI: G. Soucail). The <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$54^{\\prime \\prime }\\times 54^{\\prime \\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>54<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;54<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> field of view of the integral field unit (IFU; composed of 6400 fibers, split into four quadrants feeding the four VIMOS CCDs) was centered on the cD galaxy. In the given configuration, the spectral resolution is about 200, and the diameter of the fibers is 0.66<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>, covering the wavelength range 3900&ndash;6800 &Aring; with a dispersion of 5.355 &Aring; per pixel; <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2\\times 2.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2&amp;times;2.4</F></FORMULA>--> ks of integration time were acquired without dithering.</p>\n<p>These three&hyphen;dimensional (3D) spectroscopic data have been reduced using the Vimos Interactive Pipeline Graphical Interface (VIPGI; Scodeggio et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf58\">2005</xref>).<xref ref-type=\"fn\" rid=\"fn11\">11</xref> Before building the data cube for each exposure, every step in the data reduction was performed on a single&hyphen;quadrant basis. After bias subtraction and cosmic&hyphen;ray removal (see Zanichelli et al. [<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf71\">2005</xref>] for a description of the algorithm), the spectra were traced on the CCDs with the help of the high signal&hyphen;to&hyphen;noise ratio (S/N) spectra of a continuum lamp. Following wavelength calibration, inhomogeneities in fiber efficiencies were corrected by measuring the counts in the 5577 &Aring; sky emission line after subtracting the contribution from a galaxy spectrum where fibers cover a galaxy position. The flux calibration is applied by using observations of a standard star in each quadrant. See Covone et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf14\">2006</xref>), who present similar data on Abell 2667, for a detailed description of the procedures.</p>\n<fn-group>\n<fn id=\"fn11\">\n<label>11</label>\n<p>VIPGI has been developed within the VIRMOS Consortium. For more information, see <ext-link ext-link-type=\"uri\" xlink:href=\"http://cosmos.mi.iasf.cnr.it/pandora/vipgi.html\">http://cosmos.mi.iasf.cnr.it/pandora/vipgi.html</ext-link>.</p>\n</fn></fn-group>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc2.5\">\n<label>2.5.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Redshift Measurements</title>\n<p>We attempted to measure the redshift of all individual objects falling in the slits that revealed a discernible continuum or possible emission lines. To obtain an accurate redshift measurement for foreground galaxies, cluster members, and other bright objects, we applied the IRAF task <monospace>xcsao</monospace> from the radial velocity package RVSAO (Kurtz et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf41\">1992</xref>) on all extracted spectra. This procedure uses a cross&hyphen;correlation method based on spectral templates (Coleman et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf13\">1980</xref>; Kinney et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf35\">1996</xref>) to estimate the redshift and the corresponding redshift error. For the remaining objects in the spectroscopic catalog, the redshift measurement is based on the wavelength at the peak of the brightest emission line detected. In the latter case, we estimated the redshift error from the spectral dispersion. Additional uncertainties generated by the accuracy of the relative and absolute wavelength calibrations, of about 0.8 and 1.5 &Aring;, respectively, for the LRIS data, were quadratically added to the previous estimates to yield the final redshift errors.</p>\n<p>A confidence class <italic>C</italic>, ranging from 1 to 4, was assigned to each individual redshift measurement according to the prescription of Le F&egrave;vre et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf42\">1995</xref>): this corresponds to a probability level for a correct identification of 50%, 75%, 95%, and 100%, respectively. A specific value of 9 is used when only a single secure spectral feature is seen in emission. The identification of most <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;2</F></FORMULA>--> objects in the catalog is based on only a single emission line interpreted as Ly&alpha; and a confidence class of 9. However, the constraints provided by the lensing configuration in case of multiple images (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3\">&sect; 3</xref>) enable us to strengthen most of these interpretations.</p>\n<p>Multicolor photometry was performed for all sources identified in the WFPC F702W&hyphen;band and CFH12k <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;band images, using the SExtractor software (Bertin &amp; Arnouts <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf4\">1996</xref>). Total magnitudes and errors were measured on the original images without any resampling or convolution. The final spectroscopic catalog of lensed galaxies is presented in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb2\">Table 2</xref>, and individual spectra of <inline-formula><tex-math each data set. A red circle marks the location of 44 cluster members from our sample, for which we measured a spectroscopic redshift. Long&hyphen;slit and IFU pointings were mainly focused on the central region of the cluster (within &sim;80<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>) in the vicinity of the critical curves, whereas MOS surveys with LRIS probed a wider field of view of &sim;<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$6^{\\prime }\\times 8^{\\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>6<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;8<SUP>&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>-->.</p>\n<p>The redshift distribution of lensed background galaxies appears to be highly correlated. Three sources are located in the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2.63< z< 2.69$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2.63&amp;lt;z&amp;lt;2.69</F></FORMULA>--> range, two sources have <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 0.86$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;0.86</F></FORMULA>-->, and the C1 system has a <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 1.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;1.6</F></FORMULA>--> redshift similar to C0 (Smith et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf63\">2002a</xref>). Even more prominent is a group of eight sources having <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$0.62< z< 0.64$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>0.62&amp;lt;z&amp;lt;0.64</F></FORMULA>-->, which lie predominantly at the south of the cluster center and exhibit similar colors in the composite CFH12k image (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg1\">Fig. 1</xref>).</p>\n</sec>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc3\">\n<label>3.<x> </x></label>\n<title>CATALOG OF MULTIPLY IMAGED SYSTEMS</title>\n<p>In this section we update the catalog of multiply imaged systems in the field of Abell 68, taking into account both our new spectroscopic measures and systems without spectroscopy located on the basis of their geometric location and similar colors. For each system, we present a close&hyphen;up view from the <italic>HST R</italic> image in the bottom panels of <xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg3\">Figure 3</xref> and summarize the position, photometry, shape parameters, and magnification in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb3\">Table 3</xref>.<fig-group content-type=\"figgrp\" id=\"fg3\" position=\"float\" seq=\"3\">\n<label>Fig. 3.<x>&mdash;</x></label>\n<caption><p><italic>Top</italic>: Enlarged region of the <italic>R</italic>F702W image showing the location and morphology of the multiple&hyphen;image systems identified in the field of Abell 68. declination are degrees, arcminutes, and arcseconds. In addition to the six secured systems, C10 is included as a potential candidate (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3.1\">&sect; 3.1</xref>). Col. (1): identification; cols. (2)&ndash;(3): astrometric position (J2000.0); cols. (4)&ndash;(6): ellipse shape parameters (<italic>a</italic>, <italic>b</italic>, and \u03b8); col. (7): <italic>R</italic><sub>702W</sub> magnitude; col. (8): measured redshift; col. (9): magnification factor (in magnitudes) derived from the mass model. Bracketed values are also predictions inferred from the mass model.</p>\n<fn id=\"tb3fna\">\n<label>a</label>\n<p>Smith et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf63\">2002a</xref>).</p>\n</fn>\n</table-wrap-foot>\n</table-wrap></p>\n<sec id=\"sc3.1\">\n<label>3.1.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Morphological Identification</title>\n<p>Multiply imaged systems can be identified via a visual inspection of morphologies in the central region of the <italic>HST R</italic><sub>702W</sub> image (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg3\">Fig. 3</xref>), examined in combination with the broadband photometric catalogs. Our starting point is a detailed study of candidates identified to <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu _{702}\\sim 25$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;<INF>702</INF>&amp;sim;25</F></FORMULA>--> mag arcsec<sup>&minus;2</sup> presented by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>. This work revealed three main systems (C0a, b, c; C1a, b, c; and C2a, b), as well as 20 other possible multiply imaged candidates (C3 to C22). We adopt the same nomenclature, extending to include the new systems presented here.</p>\n<p>The three images identified as C15, C16, and C17 have been selected as <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;dropouts on the basis of color&hyphen;color diagrams combining <italic>R</italic>, <italic>I</italic>, and <italic>z</italic>&hyphen;band filters. Indeed, they are very faint in the <italic>HST</italic> image (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$R_{702}\\sim 25.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>R<INF>702</INF>&amp;sim;25.7</F></FORMULA>-->) and undetected at shorter wavelengths in the <italic>B</italic> or <italic>R</italic> band with CFH12k with a combination of red <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$( R-I) _{\\mathrm{AB}\\,}\\sim 1.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;parl0;R-I&amp;parr0;<INF><RM>AB</RM></INF>&amp;sim;1.7</F></FORMULA>--> and blue <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$( I-z) _{\\mathrm{AB}\\,}\\sim -0.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;parl0;I-z&amp;parr0;<INF><RM>AB</RM></INF>&amp;sim;-0.5</F></FORMULA>--> colors, as measured with aperture photometry on the seeing&hyphen;matched images. Such a spectral energy distribution (SED) is characteristic of galaxies in the redshift range <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$5\\lesssim z\\lesssim 6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>5&amp;lsim;z&amp;lsim;6</F></FORMULA>-->, where the Ly&alpha; break in the spectral continuum occurs between the <italic>R</italic> and <italic>I</italic> bands. The preliminary mass model (<xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc4\">&sect; 4</xref>) shows that the location of these three images is compatible with a multiply imaged source, thereby strengthening the high&hyphen;redshift interpretation. We designate this system as C15 (with the three images C15a, b, and c corresponding to C15/16/17) and confirmed that the components C15a and C15b lie at the same redshift using LRIS spectroscopy (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3.2\">&sect; 3.2</xref>).</p>\n<p>The arclet identified as C20 was serendipitously covered during the same LRIS long&hyphen;slit observation. We interpret the extended emission seen in the spectrum (<xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3.2\">&sect; 3.2</xref>) as Ly&alpha; at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=2.689$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=2.689</F></FORMULA>-->. This is also supported by the mass model, which predicts two detected counterimages with similar optical colors. We refer to this system as C20a, b, and c.</p>\n<p>Next to the C20a and C20b images, a fainter extended arc C6 was identified by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref> as a possible multiply imaged system at a similar redshift. This arc can be split into three components, C6a, b, and c.</p>\n<p>Finally, we uncovered a new lensed image, C23a, close to the cluster center during the critical line survey using LRIS (Santos et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf57\">2004</xref>). Its spectrum is consistent with a high&hyphen;redshift source dominated by its Ly&alpha; emission. Again, the cluster mass model predicts the position of a second faint component for this system (C23b), detected on the <italic>HST</italic> image.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc3.2\">\n<label>3.2.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Redshift Constraints</title>\n<p>We now present the new spectroscopic redshifts obtained for six multiply imaged candidates, as well as constraints implied for the remaining multiply imaged systems, C2 and C10, from the updated mass model (<xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc4\">&sect; 4</xref>).<list>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C0 source</italic>.&mdash;This source is a strongly lensed (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu \\sim 3.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;&amp;sim;3.2</F></FORMULA>--> mag) multiply imaged system with three components, discovered during a survey for extremely red objects (EROs) in the fields of 10 massive galaxy cluster lenses at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 0.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;0.2</F></FORMULA>--> (Smith et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf64\">2002b</xref>). A redshift measurement on the brightest image, C0a, was presented in Smith et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf63\">2002a</xref>). Based on the 4000 &Aring; break identification at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\lambda =1.04\\pm 0.01$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;lambda;=1.04&amp;plusmn;0.01</F></FORMULA>--> &mu;m, the redshift is <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=1.60\\pm 0.03$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=1.60&amp;plusmn;0.03</F></FORMULA>-->. This image was also included in two LRIS masks, but we failed to detect strong spectral features in the wavelength range 5500&ndash;9200 &Aring;.</p>\n<p>Because of the clear symmetry of images C0a and C0b with respect to the critical line, it is possible to isolate four bright knots in each of images C0a, C0b, and C0c and use the corresponding 12 images to constrain the mass model. Furthermore, part of the southwest knot of C0a is located within the radial caustic line in the source plane. We are able to detect a very faint radial arc predicted by the mass model (labeled &ldquo;C0&hyphen;radial&rdquo; in <xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg3\">Fig. 3</xref>) after removing the light from the BCG.</p>\n</list-item>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C1 source</italic>.&mdash;The brightest component C1a of this system was observed during our NIRSPEC critical lines survey (see Stark &amp; Ellis <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf65\">2006</xref>; Stark et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf66\">2007</xref>). Three strong emission lines were identified as [O <sc>iii</sc>] &lambda;5007, [O <sc>iii</sc>] &lambda;4959, and H&beta; (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg4\">Fig. 4</xref>, <italic>left</italic>), which unambiguously give the redshift <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=1.583$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=1.583</F></FORMULA>-->. Optical spectroscopy of component C1c, included in one of our LRIS masks, could not identify any strong [O <sc>ii</sc>] emission for this source, with a 3 &sigma; upper limit of 50 &Aring; for the equivalent width in the rest frame.</p>\n</list-item>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C4 source</italic>.&mdash;Although not multiply imaged, this blue arc has very strong Ly&alpha; emission corresponding to <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 2.63$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;2.63</F></FORMULA>-->. An extended Ly&alpha; blob has also been detected in the IFU data (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc5.4\">&sect; 5.4</xref>; <xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg3\">Fig. 3</xref>). The mass model gives a very high magnification factor of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu \\sim 4.0$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;&amp;sim;4.0</F></FORMULA>--> mag, because the source is very close to a cusp.</p>\n</list-item>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C6 and C20 sources</italic>.&mdash;We identify a spatially extended emission line in the LRIS spectrum at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\lambda =4485$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;lambda;=4485</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;, surrounding the C20c image (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg4\">Fig. 4</xref>, <italic>middle</italic>). The lack of other strong emission lines in the optical range and the predicted position for two other components for C20 from the mass model confirms this to be Ly&alpha; at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=2.689$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=2.689</F></FORMULA>-->. In addition, this redshift is close to the Ly&alpha; blob associated with C4, and we identify a similar strong emission line at a similar redshift, <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=2.693$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=2.693</F></FORMULA>-->, for the nearby source C25 (&sim;8<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> away in the source plane).</p>\n<p>The location and color of the lower surface brightness arc, C6, close to images C20a and C20b, is compatible with three merging images forming a single giant arc at a similar redshift (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg4\">Fig. 4</xref>, <italic>middle</italic>). This is further evidence of a possible group of galaxies at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 2.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;2.6</F></FORMULA>--> including sources C6, C20, and C25.</p>\n<p><italic>C15 source</italic>.&mdash;A strong asymmetric emission line is clearly seen on the LRIS spectrum at the position of C15a and C15b (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg4\">Fig. 4</xref>, <italic>top right</italic>), with a central peak at 7808 &Aring;. In both cases, a faint continuum is detected on the red side of the emission line, with a flux &sim;<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$( 4.4\\pm 1.5) \\times 10^{-19}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;parl0;4.4&amp;plusmn;1.5&amp;parr0;&amp;times;10<SUP>-19</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> ergs s<sup>&minus;1</sup> cm<sup>&minus;2</sup> &Aring;<sup>&minus;1</sup>. We interpret the emission line as Ly&alpha; at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.421$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.421</F></FORMULA>-->. This redshift could be slightly overestimated due to an unknown amount of self&hyphen;absorption in the Ly&alpha; emission line and the absence of other spectral features. By averaging the extracted spectra of both images (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg4\">Fig. 4</xref>, <italic>top right</italic>), the integrated flux measured within the emission line, of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$( 9.7\\pm 0.8) \\times 10^{-17}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;parl0;9.7&amp;plusmn;0.8&amp;parr0;&amp;times;10<SUP>-17</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> ergs s<sup>&minus;1</sup> cm<sup>&minus;2</sup>, corresponds to a rest&hyphen;frame equivalent width of &sim;35 &Aring;. We measure a full&hyphen;width half&hyphen;maximum of &sim;7 &Aring; when fitting the average emission line with a Gaussian profile. The strong Ly&alpha; emission line of this source seems to dominate the overall <italic>I</italic>&hyphen;band flux.</p>\n</list-item>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C23 source</italic>.&mdash;The identification of the pair of images C23a and C23b, predicted by the lensing model at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=3.1$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=3.1</F></FORMULA>-->, strengthens the Ly&alpha; interpretation for the single emission line seen in the spectrum of C23a at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\lambda =5028$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;lambda;=5028</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;. A fainter counterimage, C23c, predicted by the mass model, lies beyond the detection limit of the <italic>HST</italic> image.</p>\n</list-item>\n<list-item>\n<p><italic>C2 source</italic>.&mdash;This system is composed of two bright symmetrical images, identified close to the cluster center.
