The optical colors of this blue arc are indeed compatible with a source at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z< 2.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;lt;2.5</F></FORMULA>-->. It is probably formed by two images merging on the critical line; its shape is in agreement with predictions from the mass model. However, the low surface brightness of this arc and the lack of spectroscopic information strongly limit this interpretation, making it more uncertain than the systems previously mentioned. Therefore, we only include this source in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb3\">Table 3</xref> as a possible additional multiply imaged system. The mass model predicts a redshift of &sim;1.1, which is in very good agreement with the photometric redshift estimate of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z_{\\mathrm{phot}\\,}=1.15\\pm 0.05$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z<INF><RM>phot</RM></INF>=1.15&amp;plusmn;0.05</F></FORMULA>--> derived from the broadband colors using the Hyperz photometric redshift code (Bolzonella et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf5\">2000</xref>). A fainter counterimage (C10c) is predicted by the mass model, but remains undetected in the <italic>HST</italic> image.</p>\n</list-item>\n</list>\n<fig-group content-type=\"figgrp\" id=\"fg4\" position=\"float\" seq=\"4\">\n<label>Fig. 4.<x>&mdash;</x></label>\n<caption><p><italic>Left</italic>: NIRSPEC bidimensional spectrum of component C1a, showing the detection of three strong features identified as [O <sc>iii</sc>] and H&beta; emission lines at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=1.583$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=1.583</F></FORMULA>-->, both in positive (<italic>black</italic>) or negative (<italic>white</italic>), due to the dithering offsets used. <italic>Middle</italic>: Location of the LRIS slit and extended Ly&alpha; emission identified around image C20c (<italic>thick ellipse</italic>). Two brighter components, C20a and C20b, are predicted by the mass model, in agreement with the location of the critical line at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=2.68$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=2.68</F></FORMULA>--> (<italic>solid curve</italic>). The shape and colors of the adjacent giant arc C6 are compatible with a similar redshift, suggesting a physical connection between these two sources. <italic>Top right</italic>: Close&hyphen;up of the 2D sky&hyphen;subtracted LRIS spectrum, showing both strong emission lines seen at the position of C15a and C15b. <italic>Bottom right</italic>: Average extracted spectrum of C15, with the same wavelength range, revealing the clear asymmetrical shape of the spectral line. The relative sky background level is presented as a dotted curve.</p>\n</caption>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg4a.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg4b_online.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg4c_online.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n</fig-group></p>\n</sec>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc4\">\n<label>4.<x> </x></label>\n<title>MASS MODEL</title>\n<sec id=\"sc4.1\">\n<label>4.1.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Modeling Method</title>\n<p>Using the new redshift measurements and the identification of further multiply imaged systems, we are now in a position to considerably improve the precision of the mass model presented by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>. In doing so, we will maintain the pseudo&hyphen;isothermal elliptical mass distribution model (PIEMD; Kassiola &amp; Kovner <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf32\">1993</xref>) adopted by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref> to infer the dark matter mass distribution. This parametric method has been used for modeling galaxy clusters, as well as individual galaxies (Covone et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf14\">2006</xref>; Natarajan et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf48\">1998</xref>). It assumes each dark matter clump can be parameterized by a central position, ellipticity <italic>a</italic>/<italic>b</italic>, position angle \u03b8, central velocity dispersion &sigma;<sub>0</sub>, and two characteristic radii, <italic>r</italic><sub>core</sub> and <italic>r</italic><sub>cut</sub>. The total mass of this profile is proportional to <italic>r</italic><sub>cut</sub>&sigma;<sup>2</sup><sub>0</sub>. A more detailed discussion of the validity of this approach, in contrast to alternatives, is given by Limousin et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf45\">2007</xref>).</p>\n<p>The cluster galaxy population is incorporated into the lens model as galaxy&hyphen;scale perturbations to the cluster potential, assuming a scaling relation <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$M/ L=\\mathrm{const}\\,$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>M&amp;solm0;L=<RM>const</RM></F></FORMULA>--> (Brainerd et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf6\">1996</xref> <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>) for all <italic>r</italic><sub>core</sub>, <italic>r</italic><sub>cut</sub>, and &sigma;<sub>0</sub>. This is motivated by the similar Faber &amp; Jackson (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf20\">1976</xref>) scaling relation observed in elliptical galaxies. Following the same procedure as Limousin et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf45\">2007</xref>), we keep the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$r^{*}_{\\mathrm{cut}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>r<SUP>*</SUP><INF><RM>cut</RM></INF></F></FORMULA>--> and <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\sigma ^{*}_{0}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;sigma;<SUP>*</SUP><INF>0</INF></F></FORMULA>--> values corresponding to a <italic>L</italic>* elliptical galaxy as free parameters, while keeping <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$r^{*}_{\\mathrm{core}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>r<SUP>*</SUP><INF><RM>core</RM></INF></F></FORMULA>--> at 0.15 kpc. We select cluster galaxies in the field of Abell 68 by plotting the characteristic cluster red sequences <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$B-R_{702}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>B-R<INF>702</INF></F></FORMULA>--> and <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$R_{702}-K$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>R<INF>702</INF>-K</F></FORMULA>--> in two color&hyphen;magnitude diagrams, keeping the objects pertaining to both red sequences. This reduces the photometric catalog used by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>, containing 69 galaxies with <italic>K</italic>&hyphen;band photometry, to 47 cluster members. This method is more efficient than a single red sequence selection, as we did not select any of the spectroscopically confirmed background or foreground galaxies. As described in <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>, the <italic>K</italic>&hyphen;band photometry was obtained by Balogh et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf2\">2002</xref>) using GIM2D (Simard <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf61\">1998</xref>) to fit the surface brightness profiles of the cluster galaxies. This method gives more accurate results than one could obtain with SExtractor, because SExtractor usually overestimates the local background around the brightest and most extended galaxies.</p>\n<p>In a first attempt at modeling the lens, we adopted the parameters given by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>, who included two dark matter halos. We found that any attempt to reconstruct the mass distribution using a single clump was unable to reproduce the multiply imaged systems accurately, confirming the strong bimodality of this cluster. When incorporating our spectroscopically confirmed multiply imaged systems, a reoptimization is necessary. To do this, we use the new Bayesian optimization method provided by the Lenstool software<xref ref-type=\"fn\" rid=\"fn12\">12</xref> (Kneib <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf36\">1993</xref>; Jullo et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf30\">2007</xref>) so that we can derive error estimates for each optimized parameter. The software optimizes the locations of each system in the source plane, based on the following &chi;<sup>2</sup> estimator, which defines the goodness of the fit:\n<disp-formula id=\"df1\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"df1.eps\"></graphic><!--<DFORMULA ID=\"df1\"><FD><FL>&amp;chi;<SUP>2</SUP>=<SUM notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\chi ^{2}_{i}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;chi;<SUP>2</SUP><INF>i</INF></F></FORMULA>--> is the same estimator for a given multiply imaged system <italic>i</italic>, constructed by comparing the predicted positions of the <italic>N</italic> observed images in the source plane (<italic>x</italic><sub><italic>i,j</italic></sub>, <italic>y</italic><sub><italic>i,j</italic></sub>) to their barycenter (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$x^{B}_{i}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>x<SUP>B</SUP><INF>i</INF></F></FORMULA>-->, <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$y^{B}_{i}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>y<SUP>B</SUP><INF>i</INF></F></FORMULA>-->):\n<disp-formula id=\"df2\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"df2.eps\"></graphic><!--<DFORMULA ID=\"df2\"><FD><FL>&amp;chi;<SUP>2</SUP><INF>i</INF>=<FR SHAPE=\"built\"><NU>1</NU><DE>N</DE></FR><SUM ALIGN=\"c\"><LL>j=1&amp;ldots;N</LL></SUM><FR SHAPE=\"built\"><NU>&amp;parl0;x<INF>i,j</INF>-x<SUP>B</SUP><INF>i</INF>&amp;parr0;<SUP>2</SUP>+&amp;parl0;y<INF>i,j</INF>-y<SUP>B</SUP><INF>i</INF>&amp;parr0;<SUP>2</SUP></NU><DE>&amp;sigma;<SUP>2</SUP><INF><RM>pos</RM></INF></DE></FR>,</FL></FD><NO>(2)</NO></DFORMULA>--></disp-formula>\nwhere &sigma;<sub>pos</sub> is the uncertainty in measuring the position of each image in the source plane. We use a typical value of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\sigma _{I}=0.2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;sigma;<INF>I</INF>=0.2</F></FORMULA>--><sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> for the same uncertainty in the image plane and relate it to &sigma;<sub>pos</sub> with the amplification <italic>A</italic>: <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\sigma ^{2}_{I}=A\\sigma ^{2}_{\\mathrm{pos}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;sigma;<SUP>2</SUP><INF>I</INF>=A&amp;sigma;<SUP>2</SUP><INF><RM>pos</RM></INF></F></FORMULA>-->.</p>\n<p>For its important influence on the position of systems C15 and C20, we choose to optimize the velocity dispersion and the cut radius of the third brightest cluster galaxy. We also optimize the same parameters for the BCG and galaxy 106 (adjacent to image C0c) in order to match the location of all images from the C0 system.</p>\n<p>The associated reduced &chi;<sup>2</sup> is &sim;1.7, with 21 degrees of freedom, and the astrometric error on the position of the predicted multiple images is 0.37<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> in the image plane. The new parameters of the mass model are presented in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb4\">Table 4</xref>. The optimized values are slightly higher than the ones we obtain by using only their luminosity as a parameter for the gravitational potential. However, those values are not sufficiently high to propose a third dark matter clump. As additional confirmation for the quality of the mass model, we also checked that all spectroscopically confirmed background sources for which we did not identify multiple&hyphen;image systems were predicted to be singly imaged.<table-wrap id=\"tb4\" position=\"float\" seq=\"4\">\n<label>TABLE 4</label>\n<caption><title>Most Likely Parameters of the Lens Model with 1 &sigma; Error (1): Identification; cols. (2)&ndash;(3): astrometric position relative to the brightest cluster galaxy; cols. (4)&ndash;(7): PIEMD parameters; col. (8): \u03b8 orientation, increasing from north through east. Bracketed values are not optimized.</p>\n</table-wrap-foot>\n</table-wrap></p>\n<p>In comparison with the results from <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>, we have refined the mass model by increasing the number of constrained parameters from 11 to 21, while keeping a similar reduced &chi;<sup>2</sup> value. In particular, we optimized the location of the second dark matter clump, where we have the main differences in the confirmed multiply imaged systems, and constrained individual parameters for two particular galaxies, in addition to the BCG.</p>\n<fn-group>\n<fn id=\"fn12\">\n<label>12</label>\n<p>For more information and to download the latest version of the code, see <ext-link ext-link-type=\"uri\" xlink:href=\"http://www.oamp.fr/cosmology/lenstool\">http://www.oamp.fr/cosmology/lenstool</ext-link>.</p>\n</fn></fn-group>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc4.2\">\n<label>4.2.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Results from the Mass Model</title>\n<p>Our improved mass model of Abell 68 enables us to compute a <italic>lensing</italic> mass of the cluster by integrating the derived surface mass density within a given projected distance <italic>R</italic>. Within a physical radius <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$R< 500$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>R&amp;lt;500</F></FORMULA>--> kpc, we obtain a value <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$M_{\\mathrm{lens}\\,}=( 5.31\\pm 0.17) \\times 10^{14}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>M<INF><RM>lens</RM></INF>=&amp;parl0;5.31&amp;plusmn;0.17&amp;parr0;&amp;times;10<SUP>14</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub>. This is somewhat higher than the value <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$( 4.4\\pm 0.1) \\times 10^{14}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;parl0;4.4&amp;plusmn;0.1&amp;parr0;&amp;times;10<SUP>14</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub> derived by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>. By comparing both models using the individual parameters given in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb4\">Table 4</xref>, this difference arises mainly because of the higher mass of the second dark matter clump, for which we derive higher &sigma;<sub>0</sub> and <italic>r</italic><sub>cut</sub> values compared to <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>. The remaining model parameters (the location, ellipticity, and orientation) lie within 3 &sigma;. We argue that the parameters of the secondary clump are better constrained in our model, given the identification of new multiple images to the northwest of the cluster. The difference with <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref> is further revealed by computing the ratio <italic>M</italic><sub>cen</sub>/<italic>M</italic><sub>tot</sub> between the mass of the central component (with sole contributions from the main clump and the BCG) and the total mass within 500 kpc. We find <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$M_{\\mathrm{cen}\\,}/ M_{\\mathrm{tot}\\,}=0.56\\pm 0.05$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>M<INF><RM>cen</RM></INF>&amp;solm0;M<INF><RM>tot</RM></INF>=0.56&amp;plusmn;0.05</F></FORMULA>-->, lower than the value of 0.68 derived by <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>. This strengthens the bimodal nature of Abell 68. Our parameters for the individual contributing galaxies are quite similar to <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf62\">S05</xref>, except for the low <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$r^{*}_{\\mathrm{cut}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>r<SUP>*</SUP><INF><RM>cut</RM></INF></F></FORMULA>--> value, indicating that the halos have a smaller spatial extent.</p>\n<p>Within the uncertainties, we are now able to predict the location and expected fluxes of the counterimages for the observed multiple systems C2, C10, and C23. Furthermore, the model gives us an estimate of the redshift for the multiple systems C2 and C10, which do not yet have spectroscopic measurements. These predictions are summarized in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb3\">Table 3</xref> as bracketed values.</p>\n<p>In the process of the Bayesian optimization, the software computes the magnification factors and the related error estimates for each source included in the spectroscopic catalog or the multiple images catalog. These values are reported in Tables <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb2\">2</xref> and <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb3\">3</xref>, respectively.</p>\n<p>Apart from the multiple&hyphen;image systems described before, all other background sources in our spectroscopic catalog (C4, C7, C8, C12, C14, C24, C25, C26, and C27) are predicted to be singly imaged. This is compatible with our morphological data. For other sources that do not show multiple images (C3, C5, C9, C11, C13, and C18), we use the mass model to predict their maximum redshift <italic>z</italic><sub>max</sub>. As the radius of the critical line increases with source redshift <italic>z</italic><sub><italic>s</italic></sub>, a multiple image is expected if <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z_{s}> z_{\\mathrm{max}\\,}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z<INF>s</INF>&amp;gt;z<INF><RM>max</RM></INF></F></FORMULA>-->. These <italic>z</italic><sub>max</sub> values are summarized in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb3\">Table 3</xref> and are consistent with the observed optical colors. Image C18 is predicted to be a single image at any redshift.</p>\n</sec>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc5\">\n<label>5.<x> </x></label>\n<title>PHYSICAL PROPERTIES OF FAINT Ly&alpha; EMITTERS</title>\n<p>Via our spectroscopic campaign and improved mass model, we are now in a position to explore the physical properties and luminosity distribution of a large sample of intrinsically faint <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2< z< 6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2&amp;lt;z&amp;lt;6</F></FORMULA>--> sources. We recognize that the volumes sampled may be unrepresentative, but that our survey illustrates, by example, the promise of more extensive surveys that may soon be possible with larger cluster samples.</p>\n<p>First we selected from our spectroscopic catalog a subsample of seven high&hyphen;redshift sources (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 1.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;1.5</F></FORMULA>-->) that all have clearly detected Ly&alpha; emission lines. The measured rest&hyphen;frame equivalent widths <italic>W</italic> exceed 2 &Aring;, and the majority have <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$W\\gtrsim 10$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>W&amp;gsim;10</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;. By contrast, typical LAEs selected within narrowband surveys have <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$W\\gtrsim 30$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>W&amp;gsim;30</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;. The strong magnification thus gives us insight into the physical properties of these faint LAEs, including the star formation rate, the stellar mass, and the physical scale corresponding to the star&hyphen;forming regions. 5.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.6</F></FORMULA>--> found by Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>) in Abell 2218 (col. [9]). Col (1): Redshift, magnification factor &mu;, unlensed UV luminosity (<italic>L</italic><sub>&lambda;</sub>) at rest&hyphen;frame <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\lambda =1500$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;lambda;=1500</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;, observed integrated flux in the Ly&alpha; emission line, corresponding unlensed Ly&alpha; luminosity, star formation rate derived from the UV continuum (SFR<sub>UV</sub>) or the Ly&alpha; emission (SFR<sub>Ly&alpha;</sub>), stellar mass estimated from SED fitting (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc5.2\">&sect; 5.2</xref>), intrinsic physical scale <italic>R</italic> (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc5.3\">&sect; 5.3</xref>), star formation surface density &Sigma;, and specific star formation rate.</p>\n</table-wrap-foot>\n</table-wrap></p>\n<sec id=\"sc5.1\">\n<label>5.1.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Star Formation Rates</title>\n<p>We explore two ways of determining the instantaneous star formation rate (SFR) for a high&hyphen;redshift LAE, both using the calibration from Kennicutt (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf34\">1998</xref>), who assumed a Salpeter (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf55\">1955</xref>) initial mass function with mass limits 0.1 and 100 <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub>. The first calibration is based on the UV continuum luminosity <italic>L</italic><sub>1500</sub> at 1500 &Aring; in the rest frame, with the following relationship:\n<disp-formula id=\"df3\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"df3.eps\"></graphic><!--<DFORMULA ID=\"df3\"><FD><FL><RM>SFR</RM><INF><RM>UV</RM></INF>&amp;parl0;M<INF>&amp;odot;</INF>&amp;ucp.wordsp;<RM>yr</RM><SUP>-1</SUP>&amp;parr0;=1.05&amp;times;10<SUP>-40</SUP>L<INF>1500</INF>&amp;parl0;<RM>ergs</RM>&amp;ucp.wordsp;<RM>s</RM><SUP>-1</SUP>&amp;ucp.wordsp;&amp;angst;<ZW><SUP>-1</SUP>&amp;parr0;.</FL></FD><NO>(3)</NO></DFORMULA>--></disp-formula>\nWe estimated the individual <italic>L</italic><sub>1500</sub> values in this sample through the broadband photometric measurements.</p>\n<p>The second calibration adopted from Kennicutt (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf34\">1998</xref>) is based on the intrinsic luminosity within the Ly&alpha; emission line, assuming no extinction and case B recombination (Brocklehurst <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf9\">1971</xref>):\n<disp-formula id=\"df4\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"df4.eps\"></graphic><!--<DFORMULA ID=\"df4\"><FD><FL><RM>SFR</RM><INF><RM>Ly</RM>&amp;alpha;</INF>&amp;parl0;M<INF>&amp;odot;</INF>&amp;ucp.wordsp;<RM>yr</RM><SUP>-1</SUP>&amp;parr0;=9.1&amp;times;10<SUP>-43</SUP>L<INF><RM>Ly</RM>&amp;alpha;</INF>&amp;parl0;<RM>ergs</RM>&amp;ucp.wordsp;<RM>s</RM><SUP>-1</SUP>&amp;parr0;.</FL></FD><NO>(4)</NO></DFORMULA>--></disp-formula>\nThe corresponding SFR estimates are given in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb5\">Table 5</xref>. In most cases, we find good agreement between these two estimates, with a trend for SFR<sub>Ly&alpha;</sub> to be lower than SFR<sub>UV</sub>, with a mean ratio <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mathrm{SFR}\\,_{\\mathrm{UV}\\,}/ \\mathrm{SFR}\\,_{\\mathrm{Ly}\\,\\alpha }\\sim 1$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F><RM>SFR</RM><INF><RM>UV</RM></INF>&amp;solm0;<RM>SFR</RM><INF><RM>Ly</RM>&amp;alpha;</INF>&amp;sim;1</F></FORMULA>-->&ndash;4. We interpret this difference as due to the specific properties of Ly&alpha; emission, which usually shows some self&hyphen;absorption or dust extinction. The ratio above is quite similar to that typically found in high&hyphen;redshift Ly&alpha; samples, &sim;3 (Santos et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf57\">2004</xref>; Ajiki et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf1\">2003</xref>), as well as for the most distant galaxies at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 6.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;6.5</F></FORMULA>--> (Hu et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf29\">2002</xref>; Kodaira et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf40\">2003</xref>). We note two exceptions, C27 and C25; these show much higher SFR ratios (&sim;50). Since C27 shows a double nucleus, its UV emission may be coming from an active galactic nucleus (AGN). For C25, we estimate a 0.6<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> offset between the center of the star&hyphen;forming region and the center of the LRIS slit (originally aligned on C15a and C15b). Conceivably, we missed the majority of the light coming from this object, which may explain the discrepancy.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc5.2\">\n<label>5.2.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Stellar Masses</title>\n<p>Next we combine the constraints from multiband photometry and spectroscopic redshifts to derive estimates of the stellar mass associated with each source. A key question is whether LAEs are being seen at a special stage in their evolution, for example, with a high star formation rate, but low stellar mass. In this calculation, prior to SED fitting, it is important to remove the contribution of the Ly&alpha; flux from the photometric measurements.</p>\n<p>We derive the stellar mass using the Bayesian stellar mass code developed by Bundy et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf11\">2005</xref>), which compares the SED of each object with a grid of synthetic SEDs from Bruzual &amp; Charlot (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf10\">2003</xref>) assuming a Chabrier (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf12\">2003</xref>) initial mass function. The star formation history is parameterized as an exponential decaying burst <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mathrm{SFR}\\,\\propto \\mathrm{exp}\\,\\left(-t/ \\tau \\right)$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F><RM>SFR</RM>&amp;prop;<RF>exp</RF><FEN LP=\"PAR\" STYLE=\"S\">-t&amp;solm0;&amp;tau;<RP POST=\"PAR\" STYLE=\"S\"></FEN></F></FORMULA>-->. In addition, the code gives an error estimate for each stellar mass, combining photometric errors and degeneracies in the model parameter space (age, reddening, metallicity, and star formation history). At <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2\\lesssim z\\lesssim 5.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2&amp;lsim;z&amp;lsim;5.5</F></FORMULA>-->, photometric measurements or upper limits in the seven filters from <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb6\">Table 6</xref> cover the rest&hyphen;frame UV and optical wavelengths, which is the main limiting factor in deriving stellar masses. Depending on the number of photometric bands (2&ndash;7) where a LAE is detected, the typical errors arising from the degeneracies in model parameters cover the range 0.1&ndash;0.5 in <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mathrm{log}\\,M_{*}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F><RF>log</RF>M<INF>*</INF></F></FORMULA>-->. It was not possible to derive a stellar mass for C26, because it is only detected in the <italic>R</italic><sub>F702W</sub> filter.<table-wrap id=\"tb6\" position=\"float\" seq=\"6\">\n<label>TABLE 6</label>\n<caption><title>Broadband Photometry of the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.6</F></FORMULA>--> Galaxy Discovered by Ellis et al.</title></caption>\n<graphic xlink:href=\"tb6.eps\" position=\"float\"></graphic>\n<oasis:table frame=\"topbot\" colsep=\"0\" rowsep=\"2\" pgwide=\"1\"
