NICMOS and <italic>Spitzer</italic> IRAC images.</p>\n</table-wrap-foot>\n</table-wrap></p>\n<p>Stellar masses, corrected for magnification, are reported in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb5\">Table 5</xref>. We also compute the inverse of the specific star formation rate (star formation rate per unit stellar mass (e.g., Brinchmann et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf7\">2004</xref>), based on the SFR<sub>UV</sub> estimate. This gives an indication of the timescale on which the star formation is taking place in each object. We find typical values of 500 Myr to 1 Gyr, suggesting that higher star formation may have occurred in these LAEs during the past, unless they were formed very early.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc5.3\">\n<label>5.3.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Physical Scales</title>\n<p>In addition to brightening the observed flux of background sources, the magnification also stretches the angular sizes of the lensed images. This affects all the object shape parameters (<italic>a</italic>, <italic>b</italic>, and \u03b8), increasing the observed solid angle by the same factor &mu;. We are thus able to probe a physical scale <italic>R</italic> in the source plane, with\n<disp-formula id=\"df5\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"df5.eps\"></graphic><!--<DFORMULA ID=\"df5\"><FD><FL>R=<RAD><RCD>ab/&amp;mu;</RCD></RAD>D<INF><RM>A</RM></INF>&amp;parl0;z&amp;parr0;,</FL></FD><NO>(5)</NO></DFORMULA>--></disp-formula>\nwhere <italic>D</italic><sub>A</sub>(<italic>z</italic>) is the angular distance for a source at <italic>z</italic>.</p>\n<p>For most of the high&hyphen;redshift sources that are not resolved (along one direction) in the <italic>HST</italic> image, this value of <italic>R</italic> is an upper limit (<xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb5\">Table 5</xref>). In most cases, we find that we are able to probe high&hyphen;redshift sources at sub&hyphen;kiloparsec scales. Another interesting physical property we derive is the intrinsic surface density of star formation [<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\Sigma =\\mathrm{SFR}\\,_{\\mathrm{UV}\\,}/ ( \\pi R^{2}) $\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;Sigma;=<RM>SFR</RM><INF><RM>UV</RM></INF>&amp;solm0;&amp;parl0;&amp;pi;R<SUP>2</SUP>&amp;parr0;</F></FORMULA>-->], which is a lower limit when sources are unresolved.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc5.4\">\n<label>5.4.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Ly&alpha; Emission Surrounding C4</title>\n<p>We now turn to a specific issue relating to the origin of the so&hyphen;called Ly&alpha; blobs, of which C4 at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=2.63$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=2.63</F></FORMULA>--> is the first lensed example. We have used the updated mass model to reconstruct the source&hyphen;plane morphology of C4. The high magnification (&sim;4 mag) enables us to resolve the source morphology at &sim;30 pc scales. The galaxy displays a bright component with an intrinsic elongated shape and several knots, at a scale length of &sim;3 kpc along the major axis. A fainter component having a similar shape and one bright knot is located &sim;4.6 kpc away (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg5\">Fig. 5</xref>, <italic>fourth panel</italic>). Such an elongated shape and small physical scale is not uncommon among high&hyphen;redshift galaxies: Ravindranath et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf53\">2006</xref>) have measured that &sim;50% of galaxies in their sample of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 2.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;2.5</F></FORMULA>--> Lyman break galaxies (LBGs) taken from GOODS show a barlike morphology and scale lengths of about 1.7&ndash;2. kpc.<fig-group content-type=\"figgrp\" id=\"fg5\" position=\"float\" seq=\"5\">\n<label>Fig. 5.<x>&mdash;</x></label>\n<caption><p><italic>Left</italic>: Negative color image of a 40<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup> per side region around the source C4, produced by combining three different wavelength slices from the IFU data cube, a 15 &Aring; wide region encompassing the Ly&alpha; emission (<italic>blue</italic>)and two broad&hyphen;wavelength regions at redder wavelengths (<italic>green and red</italic>). The extended emission around the arc C4 is clearly detected in the blue frame. <italic>Right</italic>: Ly&alpha; emission properties of C4 observed with the IFU data. <italic>Left to right</italic>, Rest&hyphen;frame equivalent&hyphen;width mapping of the Ly&alpha; emission (with corresponding color scale), contours of Ly&alpha; emission overplotted on the <italic>HST</italic> image, and <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;band reconstruction of C4 in the source plane.</p>\n</caption>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg5a_online.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg5b_online.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n</fig-group></p>\n<p>The strong Ly&alpha; emission of C4 detected with LRIS was also identified in the VIMOS/IFU data (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg5\">Fig. 5</xref>, <italic>first panel</italic>). Compared with the observed size of the arc in the continuum image <italic>R</italic><sub>702</sub> (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$4^{\\prime \\prime }\\times 1.2^{\\prime \\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>4<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;1.2<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>-->), this emission is significantly more extended (&sim;<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$15^{\\prime \\prime }\\times 3^{\\prime \\prime }$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>15<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP>&amp;times;3<SUP>&amp;prime;&amp;prime;</SUP></F></FORMULA>-->; <xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg5\">Fig. 5</xref>, <italic>third panel</italic>). After correction for an average magnification, this corresponds to an intrinsic scale of &sim;10 kpc.</p>\n<p>We use the <italic>R</italic><sub>702W</sub> image to estimate the continuum flux of C4 at the wavelength of the Ly&alpha; emission, after applying a <italic>k</italic>&hyphen;correction factor assuming a UV spectral slope of 2.0 typical of starburst galaxies. By comparing the spatial coverage of the Ly&alpha; emission and the continuum, we construct a map of rest&hyphen;frame Ly&alpha; equivalent width <italic>W</italic><sub>0</sub> (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg5\">Fig. 5</xref>, <italic>second and third panels</italic>). The <italic>W</italic><sub>0</sub> values are typically in the range <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$5< W_{0}< 10$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>5&amp;lt;W<INF>0</INF>&amp;lt;10</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring; in the region detected on the <italic>HST</italic> image. However, the map shows a significant increase of Ly&alpha; equivalent width, with values <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$W_{0}> 10$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>W<INF>0</INF>&amp;gt;10</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;, in the northern part of the arc, where the continuum is hardly visible in <italic>R</italic> band. Because of the size of the blob and the presence of this stronger stellar continuum at the center of C4, the most probable mechanism producing such an extended Ly&alpha; emission is the presence of a superwind outflow originating from the central starburst (Taniguchi et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf69\">2001</xref>; Wilman et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf70\">2005</xref>).</p>\n<p>We also observed C4 with two different LRIS configurations, located across or along the longer dimension of the arc (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg6\">Fig. 6</xref>). In both cases, we observed two different components to the Ly&alpha; line on the two&hyphen;dimensional (2D) spectrum, a stronger emission centered around 4411 &Aring; and a fainter emission region at a slightly bluer wavelength (4408 &Aring;). The LRIS data also show a tilt in the emission region, due to an offset in the central peak of the Ly&alpha; line (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg6\">Fig. 6</xref>, <italic>top</italic>). These components may be related to the different star&hyphen;forming regions identified morphologically in the <italic>HST</italic> image. Unfortunately, because of the poorer resolution, no similar offset in the central wavelength or variations in the line profile were detected in the IFU data.<fig-group content-type=\"figgrp\" id=\"fg6\" position=\"float\" seq=\"6\">\n<label>Fig. 6.<x>&mdash;</x></label>\n<caption><p>LRIS observations of C4. <italic>Left</italic>: Close&hyphen;ups of each 2D spectrum showing the two components appearing in the Ly&alpha; emission. <italic>Right</italic>: Corresponding LRIS slit configuration plotted over the <italic>HST</italic> image.</p>\n</caption>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg6.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n</fig-group></p>\n<p>The main difference between C4 and the very luminous Ly&alpha; blobs is its very small physical size, 2.2 kpc, compared with the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$R> 30$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>R&amp;gt;30</F></FORMULA>--> kpc selection criteria for Ly&alpha; blobs adopted by Matsuda et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf46\">2004</xref>), along with the rest&hyphen;frame equivalent&hyphen;width criterion <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$W_{0}> 20$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>W<INF>0</INF>&amp;gt;20</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;. For this reason, it is more likely that the associated physical processes may be different, the size of C4 being more similar to extended Ly&alpha; emssions observed around star&hyphen;forming galaxies. In this strongly lensed case, the effects of outflows on the Ly&alpha; emission can be studied in higher detail by way of the lensing magnification, stretching the observed scales.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc5.5\">\n<label>5.5.<x> </x></label>\n<title>Intrinsic Properties of the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.4</F></FORMULA>--> Source</title>\n<p>We finally turn to the most distant lensed source, C15, at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.4</F></FORMULA>--> and whether it is a further example of the intriguing lensed source detected at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=5.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=5.6</F></FORMULA>--> by Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>) in Abell 2218. C15 has an intrinsic Ly&alpha; luminosity of &sim;<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$3\\times 10^{42}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>3&amp;times;10<SUP>42</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> ergs s<sup>&minus;1</sup>. This is about 5 times fainter than typical values found for <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.7</F></FORMULA>--> LAEs targeted by narrowband searches (Hu et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf28\">2004</xref>; Shimasaku et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf60\">2006</xref>), but not too dissimilar to those in the much fainter <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 6.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;6.5</F></FORMULA>--> sample from Kashikawa et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf31\">2006</xref>), who used very deep (&sim;10 ks) spectroscopy with Keck and Subaru to confirm 17 faint LAEs.</p>\n<p>All three images of this source are unresolved along the shear direction and therefore suggest a very small physical scale, <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$R\\lesssim 300$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>R&amp;lsim;300</F></FORMULA>--> pc, in the source plane. More interestingly, we infer a minimum star formation surface density of &sim;16 <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub> kpc<sup>&minus;2</sup>, which is much higher than for any other object in our sample, making this source similar to the most active star&hyphen;forming regions at any redshift.</p>\n<p>The strong Ly&alpha; emission dominates the optical flux, and in this respect it is very similar to the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.6</F></FORMULA>--> object found by Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>) in the cluster Abell 2218. To compare these sources, we have performed a reanalysis of the photometric data for that object, taking into account <italic>HST</italic> data that arrived for Abell 2218 subsequent to the Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>) analysis. This includes <italic>HST</italic> ACS, NICMOS, and <italic>Spitzer</italic> IRAC observations presented by Kneib et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf37\">2004</xref>) and Egami et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf18\">2005</xref>). We find that the Ellis et al. source is now detected in the <italic>I</italic><sub>F814W</sub>, <italic>z</italic><sub>F850LP</sub>, <italic>J</italic><sub>F110W</sub>, and <italic>H</italic><sub>160W</sub> filters (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg7\">Fig. 7</xref>; <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb6\">Table 6</xref>). The source is faint (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mathrm{AB}\\,\\sim 26.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F><RM>AB</RM>&amp;sim;26.6</F></FORMULA>-->) and remains undetected with IRAC at 3.6 and 4.5 &mu;m. However, the IRAC upper limits are quite high (around <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mathrm{AB}\\,\\sim 24$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F><RM>AB</RM>&amp;sim;24</F></FORMULA>-->), due to the proximity of the BCG (&sim;15<sup><inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\arcsec$\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula></sup>) and a coarse point&hyphen;spread function.<fig-group content-type=\"figgrp\" id=\"fg7\" position=\"float\" seq=\"7\">\n<label>Fig. 7.<x>&mdash;</x></label>\n<caption><p><italic>HST</italic> broadband detections of the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.6</F></FORMULA>--> pair found by Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>) in Abell 2218. <italic>Left to right</italic>, <italic>I</italic><sub>F814W</sub>, <italic>z</italic><sub>850LP</sub>, <italic>J</italic><sub>F110W</sub>, and <italic>H</italic><sub>F160W</sub>. North is up, and east is left. The light from the nearby BCG (located toward the lower right corner) has been subtracted from the NICMOS data for clarity.</p>\n</caption>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg7.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n</fig-group></p>\n<p>In order to compare the revised data with that for C15, we compute and incorporate in column (9) of <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb5\">Table 5</xref> various physical properties for the Ellis et al. object, alongside those for the other LAEs. When deriving the stellar mass, we note the significant change implied by the new data (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$M_{*}\\sim 10^{8}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>M<INF>*</INF>&amp;sim;10<SUP>8</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub>; cf. 10<sup>6</sup>&ndash;10<sup>7</sup> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub> given by Ellis et al.). The major change arises from different assumptions: in order to reproduce the observed Ly&alpha; emission and the nondetection of the UV spectral continuum in LRIS, Ellis et al. used the Starburst99 spectrophotometric code (Leitherer et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf44\">1999</xref>) to derive an upper limit of 2 Myr on the age of the source, assuming a constant SFR and no extinction.</p>\n<p>Although the new <italic>HST</italic> photometry of this object is restricted to the rest&hyphen;frame wavelength <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\lambda < 2500$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;lambda;&amp;lt;2500</F></FORMULA>--> &Aring;, the SED&hyphen;fitting method used in our reanalysis should be more reliable, because it is based on fewer assumptions, especially regarding the star formation history. Our best SED&hyphen;fitting model also predicts <italic>Spitzer</italic> IRAC continuum fluxes consistent with the nondetection of this pair in the 3.6 and 4.5 &mu;m bands.</p>\n<p>Compared with the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.6</F></FORMULA>--> galaxy from Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>), C15 is less magnified and is intrinsically more luminous and more massive, although with a similar physical size. The mass model predicts the source to be located &sim;2.4 kpc from the caustic line in the source plane. This suggests that we are actually seeing a true small isolated object, since any similarly bright region close to C15 would also be highly magnified and multiply imaged.</p>\n<p>Another difference between the two sources arises from the rest&hyphen;frame UV stellar continuum, which is detected in the LRIS spectrum of the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.4</F></FORMULA>--> source redward of the Ly&alpha; emission. Running the Starburst99 code on this object in a way similar to Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>), the upper limit on the age is much larger, typically 50&ndash;100 Myr, with a constant SFR of 2.6 <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub> yr<sup>&minus;1</sup>. This gives a total mass of &sim;<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$( 1{\\mbox{--}} 3) \\times 10^{8}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;parl0;1&amp;ndash;3&amp;parr0;&amp;times;10<SUP>8</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub>, which is closer to the SED&hyphen;fitting estimate, in comparison with the source in Abell 2218.</p>\n<p>At the time of its discovery, the Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>) object revealed a very small, low&hyphen;mass (10<sup>6</sup>&ndash;10<sup>7</sup>) source at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.6</F></FORMULA>-->, which was also reported to be very young. With the new photometric reanalysis and by finding another example of a LAE with similar size and Ly&alpha; flux, it is more probable that we are observing two 10<sup>8</sup>&ndash;10<sup>9</sup> <italic>M</italic><sub>&odot;</sub> objects with very different star formation histories. The Ellis et al. source previously formed the majority of its stellar mass and is having a very young burst, whereas C15 has been forming stars for a longer timescale.</p>\n</sec>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc6\">\n<label>6.<x> </x></label>\n<title>DISCUSSION</title>\n<p>We have demonstrated in our survey of Abell 68 that, after applying magnification correction, we can reach LAEs with typical unlensed absolute AB magnitudes &sim;<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$-20< M_{\\mathrm{AB}\\,}< -16.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>-20&amp;lt;M<INF><RM>AB</RM></INF>&amp;lt;-16.5</F></FORMULA>--> in the rest&hyphen;frame UV. This is about 2 mag fainter than the UV selection criterion for typical Lyman break galaxies used by Steidel et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf68\">2003</xref>) of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$R_{\\mathrm{AB}\\,}< 25.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>R<INF><RM>AB</RM></INF>&amp;lt;25.5</F></FORMULA>--> at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 3$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;3</F></FORMULA>--> and the faintest LAEs found with narrowband searches (e.g., Fynbo et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf23\">2003</xref>; Gawiser et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf26\">2006</xref>; Shimasaku et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf60\">2006</xref>). Moreover, the lensed Ly&alpha; sources have much lower equivalent widths, similar to those seen in LBGs (Shapley et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf59\">2003</xref>).</p>\n<p>The derived properties of the LAEs depend on the individual magnification factors &mu; used to correct each image for the lensing effects. The error estimates on &mu;, computed by the Bayesian optimization method, range from 1% to 16% and were quadratically added to the measurement errors in <xref ref-type=\"table\" rid=\"tb5\">Table 5</xref>, in the case of <italic>L</italic><sub>Ly&alpha;</sub>, SFR<sub>Ly&alpha;</sub>, and <italic>M</italic><sub>*</sub>. In each case, the photometry is the dominant source of error. We acknowledge that these values of &mu; still depend on the approach used to parameterize the mass model, for instance, the use of the PIEMD profile for the dark matter halos. Nevertheless, the LAEs presented here are strongly lensed and have been identified in the central regions of the cluster, where the magnification factors are associated with the location of the critical lines. These critical lines are constrained by the same set of multiple images, quite independently of the parameterization used for the mass model (PIEMD or Navarro&hyphen;Frenk&hyphen;White [NFW] profile). Therefore, we are confident that the computed magnification factors are reliable.</p>\n<p>Although such a lensing survey is not strictly flux limited, we can use this unique probe to gauge the properties of the faintest LAEs yet located at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 2$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;2</F></FORMULA>-->. We find that the typical stellar masses are <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mathrm{log}\\,( M_{*}/ M_{\\odot }) \\sim 8.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F><RF>log</RF>&amp;parl0;M<INF>*</INF>&amp;solm0;M<INF>&amp;odot;</INF>&amp;parr0;&amp;sim;8.5</F></FORMULA>-->&ndash;9.5. These values are similar to the typical stellar masses of the bright LAEs from Gawiser et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf26\">2006</xref>) found by selecting very high equivalent width (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$W_{0}> 150$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>W<INF>0</INF>&amp;gt;150</F></FORMULA>-->) LAEs at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z=3.1$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z=3.1</F></FORMULA>-->. Our LAEs have fainter UV and Ly&alpha; luminosities and therefore a lower SFR, by typically 1&ndash;2 mag. Even if the wavelength range covered by the broadband photometry dominates the errors in the stellar masses derived in both surveys, this is indicative that, at comparable stellar masses, our LAEs are more quiescent than the objects found in narrowband searches.</p>\n<p>Recognizing the limitations of our sample, as a point of illustration, we compare in <xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg8\">Figure 8</xref> the luminosity range of our lensed emitters with current constraints on the cumulative Ly&alpha; luminosity function at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 3$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;3</F></FORMULA>-->, mostly based on narrowband searches. The number of dedicated searches for LAEs at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 3$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;3</F></FORMULA>--> from the literature is quite limited. We report in this diagram the compilation of five samples, either in blank fields or overdense environments, presented by Fynbo et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf24\">2001</xref>), as well as an estimate of the number density from a Ly&alpha; survey in the GOODS&hyphen;South field (Nilsson et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf49\">2006</xref>, <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf50\">2007</xref>). Based on our subsample of six emitters at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2\\lesssim z\\lesssim 3.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2&amp;lsim;z&amp;lsim;3.7</F></FORMULA>--> and the surface area probed in the high&hyphen;magnification region (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu > 0.75$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;&amp;gt;0.75</F></FORMULA>--> mag) of the source plane, we estimate a number density of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$4.3^{+2.6}_{-1.7}\\times 10^{-3}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>4.3<SUP>+2.6</SUP><INF>-1.7</INF>&amp;times;10<SUP>-3</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> Mpc<sup>&minus;3</sup> down to <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$L=1.4\\times 10^{41}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>L=1.4&amp;times;10<SUP>41</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> ergs s<sup>&minus;1</sup>. Because our spectroscopy is only sparsely covered this region, we report this value as a lower limit in <xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg8\">Figure 8</xref>. Although we acknowledge the limits due to very small statistics and the small areas probed in these lensed surveys, our sample of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 3$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;3</F></FORMULA>--> emitters gives constraints at fainter luminosities than any of the narrowband searches at this redshift. More observations are, however, needed in order to better constrain the faint&hyphen;end slope of this luminosity function.<fig-group content-type=\"figgrp\" id=\"fg8\" position=\"float\" seq=\"8\">\n<label>Fig. 8.<x>&mdash;</x></label>\n<caption><p>Cumulative luminosity function of Ly&alpha; emitters (LAEs). Red data points are <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 3$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;3</F></FORMULA>--> estimates from Fynbo et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf24\">2001</xref>), either in overdense regions (<italic>open circles</italic>) or blank fields (<italic>crosses</italic>). We also give recent results at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 3.1$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;3.1</F></FORMULA>--> from a Ly&alpha; survey in GOODS&hyphen;South (Nilsson et al. <xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf50\">2007</xref>). Black data points correspond to the compilation of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5</F></FORMULA>--> surveys from Santos et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf57\">2004</xref>), and black curves are more recent fits to the <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.7</F></FORMULA>--> luminosity function by Shimasaku et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf60\">2006</xref>). We overplot in blue the number density estimates based on the sample of six LAEs at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$1.7< z< 3.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>1.7&amp;lt;z&amp;lt;3.7</F></FORMULA>-->.</p>\n</caption>\n<fig position=\"float\" fig-type=\"figure\">\n<graphic xlink:href=\"fg8_online.eps\" rotation=\"0\"></graphic>\n</fig>\n</fig-group></p>\n<p>An interesting question is the likelihood of finding highly magnified sources at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.5</F></FORMULA>--> like C15 and the source reported by Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>): we can estimate this through the space density of <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;dropouts in our magnified field of view. Based on our photometric <italic>RIz</italic> color&hyphen;color selection technique (see <xref ref-type=\"sec\" rid=\"sc3.1\">&sect; 3.1</xref>), we identified one source in the field of view covered by the <italic>HST</italic> image. Since it is detected at &sim;8 &sigma; level in the <italic>I</italic>&hyphen;band filter, where <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;dropouts are brighter, and has a magnification factor of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu \\sim 2.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;&amp;sim;2.5</F></FORMULA>-->, we computed the effective covolume in the source plane having <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$\\mu > 0.75$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>&amp;mu;&amp;gt;0.75</F></FORMULA>-->, taking into account the reduction of the surface area due to lensing effects. We derive an effective covolume of 420 Mpc<sup>3</sup>, in the redshift range <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$5< z< 6$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>5&amp;lt;z&amp;lt;6</F></FORMULA>--> probed by our set of filters. Assuming Poisson noise statistics, we obtain a rough estimate of <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2.4^{+5.4}_{-2.0}\\times 10^{-3}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2.4<SUP>+5.4</SUP><INF>-2.0</INF>&amp;times;10<SUP>-3</SUP></F></FORMULA>--> Mpc<sup>&minus;3</sup> for the number counts of <italic>R</italic>&hyphen;dropouts. Although cosmic variance effects can be quite large when probing such a small volume, this result is in good agreement with the space density of low&hyphen;luminosity Ly&alpha; sources at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5</F></FORMULA>--> on the diagram (<xref ref-type=\"fig\" rid=\"fg8\">Fig. 8</xref>) mentioned above.</p>\n<p>From these simple calculations, C15 does not seem to be a serendipitous case of a low&hyphen;luminosity <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5</F></FORMULA>--> LAE, since we would expect to find one such source in the magnified region of the cluster. By observing a larger number of lensed fields, such as the new <italic>HST</italic> clusters imaged by ACS, we could build a more significant sample of similar objects and compare their physical properties.</p>\n</sec>\n<sec id=\"sc7\">\n<label>7.<x> </x></label>\n<title>CONCLUSIONS</title>\n<p>We have performed a spectroscopic analysis of background sources in the field of the massive cluster Abell 68 and identified 26 lensed images in the range <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$0.3< z< 5.5$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>0.3&amp;lt;z&amp;lt;5.5</F></FORMULA>-->, including seven LAEs at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z> 1.7$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;gt;1.7</F></FORMULA>-->. Using the new redshift measurements and identification of new multiple&hyphen;image systems, we perform a precise modeling of the cluster mass distribution with five spectroscopic systems and also predict the redshift and counterimages for two remaining systems. This makes Abell 68 one of the best modeled lensing clusters, along with Abell 1689 and Abell 2218, allowing for the precise measurement of its dark matter distribution.</p>\n<p>We derived the star formation rates, stellar masses, and physical scales for our sample of high&hyphen;redshift LAEs. The broadband luminosities of these objects are comparable to the faint LAEs found in deep narrowband searches, but their equivalent widths are much lower, making them 1&ndash;2 mag fainter in Ly&alpha; luminosity. Two of these sources show a more extended Ly&alpha; emission region, when compared to the stellar continuum in the <italic>HST</italic> image. For one of them, we demonstrated how we use IFU data to probe regions with distinct Ly&alpha; equivalent widths. The stretch provided by lensing enables us to characterize small regions of Ly&alpha; emission that would otherwise be beyond the reach of ground&hyphen;based integral field instruments. Although the large equivalent widths are comparable to giant Ly&alpha; blobs observed around massive forming galaxies, we interpret the small physical scales of these lensed emissions as outflows originating from a central starburst.</p>\n<p>The highest redshift (<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 5.4$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;5.4</F></FORMULA>-->) multiple&hyphen;image source of this sample is very similar to the pair of strongly lensed images identified by Ellis et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf19\">2001</xref>) in Abell 2218, in terms of magnification and physical size, albeit being intrinsically more massive and more luminous. We therefore expect to detect it in IRAC images of depth similar to the data presented in Egami et al. (<xref ref-type=\"bibr\" rid=\"rf18\">2005</xref>) in the first two channels of this instrument. Such measurements would tighten the constraints on the stellar mass of this source by reducing the degeneracies in the other model parameters and also provide additional information on its age and star formation history, when combined with the properties of the Ly&alpha; emission.</p>\n<p>Our survey provides the first tentative indications of the density of faint LAEs at <inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$z\\sim 3$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>z&amp;sim;3</F></FORMULA>-->, down to unlensed fluxes of &sim;<inline-formula><tex-math notation=\"latex\"><![CDATA[\n\\documentclass{aastex}\n\\usepackage{amsbsy}\n\\usepackage{amsfonts}\n\\usepackage{amssymb}\n\\usepackage{bm}\n\\usepackage{mathrsfs}\n\\usepackage{pifont}\n\\usepackage{stmaryrd}\n\\usepackage{textcomp}\n\\usepackage{portland,xspace}\n\\usepackage{amsmath,amsxtra}\n\\usepackage[OT2,OT1]{fontenc}\n\\newcommand\\cyr{\n\\renewcommand\\rmdefault{wncyr}\n\\renewcommand\\sfdefault{wncyss}\n\\renewcommand\\encodingdefault{OT2}\n\\normalfont\n\\selectfont}\n\\DeclareTextFontCommand{\\textcyr}{\\cyr}\n\\pagestyle{empty}\n\\DeclareMathSizes{10}{9}{7}{6}\n\\begin{document}\n\\landscape\n$2\\times 10^{41}$\n\\end{document}]]></tex-math>\n</inline-formula><!--<FORMULA><F>2&amp;times;10<SUP>41</SUP></F></FORMULA>-->. Although our survey is not flux limited nor complete in any formal sense, the cumulative Ly&alpha; luminosity function we derive promises a dedicated search for lensed Ly&alpha; emitters through larger samples of well&hyphen;mapped clusters now being surveyed with <italic>HST</italic> and the ability of this approach to complement narrowband searches carried out in blank fields.</p>\n</sec>\n</body>\n<back>\n<ack>\n<sec>\n<title></title><p>We thank the anonymous referee for his/her helpful comments, and acknowledge helpful discussions with Johan Fynbo, Kim Nilsson, Fabrice Lamareille, Mark Swinbank, and Tommaso Treu. J. R. is grateful to Caltech for financial support. The Dark Cosmology Centre is funded by the Danish National Research Foundation. The authors recognize and acknowledge the very significant cultural role and reverance that the summit of Mauna Kea has always had within the indigenous Hawaiian community. We are most fortunate to have the opportunity to conduct observations from this mountain.</p>\n</sec>\n</ack>\n<ref-list type=\"unparsed\">\n<title>REFERENCES</title>\n<ref id=\"rf1\">\n<citation>Ajiki, M., et al. 2003, AJ, 126, 2091</citation>\n</ref>\n<ref id=\"rf2\">\n<citation>Balogh, M.
